- **2026-05-03 · M14.4.a** Per-extraction chat (the workspace pivot). **Why**: the whole M14 product position pivots on this. Without chat, Lucid is a one-shot summarizer — drop a doc, read the dossier, leave. With chat, Lucid is where you keep documents you're working through — drop a doc, read the dossier, ask follow-ups, draft your response, stress-test with what-ifs, come back tomorrow. Workspace > destination. Justifies the Pro/Team plan tiers from the M14.0 quota decision (chat unlimited on Pro, 50/mo on Starter, ingest-only on Free). **Backend** ([db/models.ChatMessage](backend/db/models.py), [services/chat.py](backend/services/chat.py), [routers/chat.py](backend/routers/chat.py)): new `ChatMessage` table — `(extraction_id, user_id, role, content, model_used, input_tokens, output_tokens, created_at)`. `chat_stream()` is a sync generator with the same SSE event shape as the dossier streamer (start / text / complete / error). Architecture decision: NO RAG / embeddings for v1 — stuff the entire `raw_text` + a compact dossier digest into every call. The full dossier JSON can be 15k+ tokens of prose Claude already wrote; we don't re-feed that. Instead a `_dossier_digest()` helper extracts just the high-signal bits — overture, brief, key numbers, 5W1H, assumptions, inversion, negative space, action items, open decisions — capped at ~2k tokens. System block is `cache_control: ephemeral` so messages 2+ within 5 minutes hit prompt cache (~10× cheaper than the first message). Default model = Sonnet 4.6 (cheaper / faster, plenty smart for Q&A over an already-extracted doc; users can BYOK + override later). Routes: `GET /api/extractions/{id}/chat` (list thread), `POST /api/extractions/{id}/chat` (persist user msg → stream assistant via SSE → persist assistant on `complete`), `DELETE /api/extractions/{id}/chat` (clear thread). Same `_owned_extraction` ownership check + `_protected_deps` auth posture as the rest of /api/extractions. Mock mode (no API key) returns a placeholder reply so the UI renders end-to-end without Claude calls. **Frontend** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js), [components/dossier/ChatPanel.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/ChatPanel.jsx), [components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx), [styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)): new `api.js` helpers — `listChatMessagesApi` / `sendChatMessageStream` (SSE consumer with onText / onComplete callbacks) / `clearChatApi`. New `ChatPanel.jsx` (~280 lines) is a fixed-position pane bottom-right of the studio, two states: collapsed pill (`💬 Ask anything about this document`, always visible) and expanded panel (header with Clear / Close, message list with auto-scroll-to-bottom, starter chip row when thread is empty, input form). Streaming text grows in a "live" assistant bubble with a blinking cursor (new `@keyframes blink` in styles.css); on `complete` the bubble is replaced with the persisted message from the server response. Enter to send (Shift+Enter for newline). Stop button mid-stream uses AbortController. **Three starter prompts as one-click chips** — `Draft response` / `Meeting prep` / `What if` — fire pre-templated questions through the same chat pipeline (drafters as prompt templates, not separate routes — M14.4.b can promote them to dedicated UIs if usage warrants). Loads thread history when the panel first opens for an extraction; clears state when extractionId changes. Mounted in DossierPane as a fixed-position overlay so it never affects dossier scroll layout. **Trade-offs**: full-doc-in-prompt scales to ~200k token docs comfortably (Claude 1M window, prompt cached); above that we'll need real chunk + retrieval — but the public `chat_stream` signature stays the same so it's a backend swap. Persistence is per-(user, extraction) so two viewers of a shared extraction would have separate threads; that's the privacy-conservative default and matches comments / unread tracking. Drafters are templated prompts not a structured-output schema — they produce free-text replies, not e.g. a Jira-ready ticket. Cost: each chat message charges full doc as input tokens on first call (~$0.50 for a 100k doc on Sonnet), then cached at ~$0.05 on follow-ups within 5 min. Gated by plan tier (Pro = unlimited per M14.0). **Build**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. End-to-end smoke confirmed mock chat streaming yields `[text, complete]` and ChatMessage round-trips correctly. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drop a doc → wait for dossier → click "💬 Ask anything" pill bottom-right → confirm panel expands → click "Draft response" starter → confirm user message renders + assistant streams in with blinking cursor → reload page → confirm thread persists → click Clear → confirm wiped → click ✕ → confirm collapsed pill returns).
- **2026-05-03 · M14.3.a** Structured extracts — Numbers / Timeline / Negative Space slot into the dossier story arc. **Why**: M14.1 + M14.2 made the dossier readable and verifiable; M14.3 makes it scannable. The narrative sections are great prose; readers want a numbers table they can ctrl-F, a timeline they can wall-pin, and a "what's missing" gap-list they can grill the doc author with. **Backend** ([services/lenses/dossier.py](backend/services/lenses/dossier.py)): three new Pydantic models (`NumbersExtract` with categorized facts including source-quote field; `Timeline` with ordered phase list; `NegativeSpace` with missing-item + why-it-matters pairs) added as top-level fields on `DocumentDossier`. Six new bridges inserted at exactly the right narrative points so the story arc still reads coherently: Brief→Numbers→TLDR (numbers anchor the brief in concrete scale before the longer summaries land); Domain→Timeline→Systems (Domain is static anatomy, Timeline is temporal, Systems is interactive — natural sequence); Inversion→NegativeSpace→Better Questions (stress-test → gap audit → next-step questions). Legacy bridges kept on the schema with `default=""` so pre-M14.3 dossier rows parse without errors. Master prompt updated with per-section rules (e.g. "pull EVERY discrete number" for NumbersExtract, "structural absences distinct from Better Questions" for NegativeSpace, "use the document's own time units" for Timeline) and an explicit "use new bridges, leave legacy empty" instruction. Mock dossier populates all three new sections. **Frontend** ([components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx)): three new section components. `NumbersExtractSection` groups facts by category (cost / time / count / percentage / other in stable order) with a sub-header per group; each row is a 3-col table — label (glossary-termified) | value (mono-font, semibold) | source (SourceQuote disclosure if present, ConfidenceBadge "Asserted" otherwise). `TimelineGantt` renders an alternating accent-toned strip of phase chips at the top showing the temporal sequence, then a numbered detail list below — bars are equal-width because we don't have date math (yet); v1 shows ORDER not duration. `NegativeSpaceGantt` uses a ∅ glyph instead of a bullet to telegraph "missing"; warn-tone disc background. **Conditional dispatch in DossierPane**: each new section renders only when its payload is non-empty; when missing (legacy dossier rows), the act falls through to the legacy single bridge so old rows look the same as before M14.3. The three insertion points are wrapped in `<>` fragments with their own bridges so the narrative flow stays seamless. **All three new sections use M14.2 annotation primitives** (`GlossaryTermified` for prose, `SourceQuote` for evidence quotes). **Trade-offs**: Timeline isn't a "real" Gantt — bars don't represent durations because we don't parse dates from the `when` field (`Weeks 0-2`, `Q1`, `Day 30` are all valid). Could add a date-parsing pass (chrono.js or similar) in M14.3.b if users push for proportional bars. NumbersExtract trusts Claude to enumerate every number — for a 50-page doc with hundreds of figures we may need a "show top N + view all" pagination. NegativeSpace is the highest-leverage of the three for vendor proposals / contracts but lowest-applicability for transcripts. The fall-through-to-legacy-bridge pattern means old dossier rows render unchanged; new dossiers get the richer flow. **Build**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. DossierPane chunk grew 22.04 KB → 27.24 KB raw (5.28 → 6.27 KB gzipped). Mock smoke confirmed all three sections parse + populate cleanly. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drop a number-heavy doc → confirm Numbers Extract table groups by category with mono values + Sourced pills → drop a project plan with phases → confirm Timeline strip + numbered detail list → drop a vendor proposal → confirm Negative Space surfaces the missing sections / clauses / safeguards).
- **2026-05-03 · M14.2.a** Dossier annotations — glossary tooltips + source provenance + confidence labels. **Why**: M14.1 shipped the dossier shape but readers had no way to verify claims (was the model citing the doc or making it up?), no help with specialist jargon (the Glossary section existed but you had to scroll back), and no fast read on which items were grounded vs synthesized. M14.2 layers all three affordances onto the existing render with zero backend / schema / prompt changes — purely client-side over the data the dossier already carries. **New primitives** ([components/dossier/annotations.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/annotations.jsx), 3 small components, ~120 lines): `<GlossaryTermified text terms>` walks `text` with a single regex built from all glossary terms (sorted DESC by length so longer terms win first — "User Story" beats "Story"; case-sensitive word-boundary match), substitutes a hover span around each match with the term's definition in the native `title` attribute. Dotted-underline + accent-tinted color signals "hover for more"; no popover library, no DOM mutation, screen-reader-friendly. Memoized per (text, terms) so render-time regex walking is cheap. `<SourceQuote text>` is a `<details>`-based disclosure — "▸ View source" link expands to show the verbatim quote in an accent-soft blockquote with a left accent border. Compact when collapsed, no impact on dossier scroll height until clicked. `<ConfidenceBadge sourced>` is a tiny uppercase pill — "✓ Sourced" in success-soft when the item has an evidence quote, "Asserted" in muted neutral when not. Title attribute carries the long-form explanation for hover. **Wiring** ([components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx)): pulled `glossaryTerms = dossier.glossary || []` once at the DossierPane top and passed it as a `terms` prop to every section component that renders prose. Sections updated: Brief.summary, TLDR Ladder rows, 5W1H cells, Domain branches points, Systems entities/flows/loops, 5 Whys (question + answer; replaced inline blockquote with `<SourceQuote>` + added `<ConfidenceBadge sourced={!!s.evidence}>`), Assumptions (assumption + risk_explanation), Inversion scenarios, Better Questions (question + why_it_matters), Action Items (action text — header now flexes with ConfidenceBadge sourced={!!a.source} + SourceQuote in cell body), Decisions Made / Open list items, What to Revisit item + why, User Stories want/so_that/criteria + replaced inline blockquote with `<SourceQuote>` + added `<ConfidenceBadge sourced={!!s.source_quote}>`. **Trade-offs**: native `title` tooltip vs custom popover — picked native for v1 because it's free, accessible, and works on mobile (long-press). Downside: minimal styling control + slow ~700ms hover delay. If users complain, swap to a small custom Tooltip primitive (Radix-style or hand-rolled) without changing the GlossaryTermified API. ConfidenceBadge is binary (sourced / asserted) rather than the trichotomy (evidenced / asserted / inferred) I originally proposed — collapsed because the binary maps cleanly to "is the source_quote field populated" without prompt changes. The richer trichotomy would need the prompt to label every item, which is M14.2.b territory if the binary signal proves insufficient. The 5 Whys section's source-quote display now lives inside `<SourceQuote>` (collapsed by default) instead of always-visible — slightly less prominent for power-readers but cleaner default for everyone else. **Build**: 4 vitest + vite clean; DossierPane chunk grew 19.25 KB → 22.04 KB raw (4.54 → 5.28 KB gzipped) for the annotation primitives + per-section prop threading. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drop a doc with jargon → confirm glossary terms get dotted underlines in Brief/TLDR/5W1H prose → hover one → confirm definition pops via native tooltip → expand a 5 Whys "▸ View source" → confirm quote appears in accent-soft blockquote → check Action Items for green "✓ Sourced" pills next to items the model cited).
- **2026-05-03 · M14.1.c** Dossier streaming + scrollspy chapter nav. **Why**: M14.1.b shipped the dossier render but the upload flow lost the live progress card — dossier uploads spent 30-60s on a blank spinner because the frontend used the non-streaming `extract()` route. The streaming endpoint `/api/extract/stream` was hard-wired to the stories pipeline. Also the M14.1.b sticky chapter nav was static — no active-chapter highlight as you scrolled. **Backend streaming** ([services/streaming_dossier.py](backend/services/streaming_dossier.py) — new, ~155 lines): `stream_dossier_extraction()` is a sync generator that uses Anthropic's `messages.stream()` with a tool-use definition (`emit_dossier`) whose `input_schema` is `DocumentDossier.model_json_schema()`. Same event shape as the stories streamer (start / usage / complete / error) so the frontend SSE consumer code path is shared — only the persistence branch differs server-side. MAX_OUTPUT_TOKENS bumped 16k → 16k (kept the same; dossier output runs ~8-15k so this fits). NO `thinking` parameter (Anthropic rejects `thinking + tool_choice={"type":"tool"}`); reasoning lift is small here because the schema constrains output anyway. Mock-mode path emits 5 fake usage ticks at thresholds matching dossier's likely shape (300 / 1500 / 4500 / 8500 / 12000 output tokens) so LoadingState's stage progression fires correctly. **Route dispatch** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): `/api/extract/stream` accepts a `lens` form param (default 'dossier' via `normalize()`); SSE generator branches on `effective_lens` to pick `stream_dossier_extraction` or `stream_extraction`, then on `complete` branches the persister to `persist_dossier_extraction` or `persist_extraction`. Both paths share the `record_usage` + `extraction_to_record` tail. **Frontend** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): `handleExtract` simplified — both lenses use `extractStream({lens})` now; the temporary M14.1.b non-streaming branch is gone. The `extract` import was unused after this change, removed. **Scrollspy** ([components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx)): IntersectionObserver tracks four chapter `<section>` ids (orient / structure / interrogate / act) with `root` set to the scroller ref (paneShell has `overflow:auto` — observing the viewport would never fire because chapters scroll inside the pane, not the page). RootMargin `-30% 0px -60% 0px` pulls the trigger zone to the top-third so a chapter activates as it scrolls past the sticky nav, not when it first peeks in from below. ChapterNav active pill gets accent-soft background + accent border + accent-ink text + bold font-weight; transitions on bg/border/color (var(--dur-fast)) so the swap is buttery. **Trade-offs**: the dossier streaming uses tool-use streaming, which means we get usage ticks but NOT visible JSON-by-JSON content streaming (would require parsing partial JSON, fragile). Functionally identical from the user's POV — they see the LoadingState fill up, then the dossier appears all at once on `complete`. Could chunk-render sections as they parse if it becomes a UX gap. Scrollspy fires only on scroll within the pane (not page scroll); since the studio pane IS the scroll surface, this is correct — but if we ever change the layout to make the page scroll instead, we'd need to swap root back to viewport. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. Dossier mock streaming yields `[usage × 5, complete]` as expected. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drop a doc on / → confirm LoadingState shows token progress (no longer blank spinner) → confirm Reading→Drafting→Composing stages tick → dossier renders → scroll down → confirm sticky nav active pill changes I → II → III → IV as you cross each Act header).
- **2026-05-03 · M14.1.b** Frontend dispatch + DossierPane renderer. **Why**: M14.1.a landed the backend (lens dispatcher, DocumentDossier schema, dossier extractor, /api/extract accepting lens param) but it was invisible — every extraction still rendered as the StoriesView. M14.1.b makes it visible: new uploads default to lens='dossier', the studio mounts DossierPane instead of the stories dual-pane experience, and the full 14-section narrated dossier renders end-to-end. **DossierPane** ([components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/dossier/DossierPane.jsx) — new, ~700 lines, lazy-loaded → 4.15 KB gzipped chunk): reads `extraction.lens_payload` (the DocumentDossier JSON the backend persisted) and renders top-to-bottom: sticky 4-chapter nav (I · II · III · IV) → Overture (italic large quote in a teal-tinted gradient card) → Act I (Brief, TLDR Ladder, 5W1H) → Act II (Glossary, Mindmap, Domain, Systems) → Act III (5 Whys, Assumptions, Inversion, Better Questions) → Act IV (Action Items, Decisions, What to Revisit, optional User Stories) → Closing line. Bridges between every section render as italic centred narrator text with thin horizontal rules. Each section is its own inline component (kept in one file for now; split if it grows past ~1k lines). **Section design highlights**: TLDR Ladder = 3 rows with mono labels (1 line / 1 paragraph / 1 page); 5W1H = 6-cell tonal grid; Mindmap = 3-level ASCII-art-style nested list with ├──/└── brackets in mono; Domain = 7-card grid with bullet points; Systems = entities + flows + feedback loops in 3 subsections; 5 Whys = numbered chain with optional source-quote blockquote; Assumptions = cards with risk-tone pills (red/amber/blue for high/med/low); Inversion = × bullet list; Action Items = owner/action/when table; UserStoriesSection = folded-in stories from M14.0 pick (b) with id badge + as-a-want-so-that + criteria + optional source quote (only renders when the model populated user_stories — non-requirements docs get no story section). **App dispatch** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): new ternary at the studio body — if `extraction.lens === 'dossier'` mount full-width DossierPane (no SourcePane / ResizeHandle / GapsRail since those are stories-shape concepts that don't apply to a dossier); otherwise existing narrow/wide stories layout. Side GapsRail also gated on `lens !== 'dossier'`. **handleExtract** branches on lens: dossier uses non-streaming `extract()` (POST /api/extract) since the streaming backend route is still wired to the stories pipeline; stories keeps `extractStream()` with usage-tick progress. Default lens hard-coded to 'dossier' for now (no UI lens picker — M14 was explicitly "no choosing"). **api.js** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): `buildExtractForm()` + `extract()` + `extractStream()` accept optional `lens` param appended to FormData. **Trade-offs**: dossier path loses the live progress card (LoadingState falls back to its indeterminate-slide animation since no usage ticks). M14.1.c will port the streaming endpoint to dossier so the existing progress card works for both lenses. Side rails (Sidebar extraction context, GapsRail) hide for dossier — comment count + version chain still work in Sidebar but the gaps badge won't show numbers (no gaps in dossier). DossierPane has no editing affordances (no inline edit, no per-section regen, no comments). Editing comes in a later phase if users want it. **Build**: 4 vitest + vite clean; new lazy chunk DossierPane-DE4q3hFH.js 18.45 KB raw / 4.15 KB gzipped. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (sign in → drop a doc on / → confirm a dossier streams in (large response, ~30-60s wait with indeterminate spinner) → confirm Overture + 4 chapters + bridges + closing all render → click any chapter pill in sticky nav → confirm scroll-to-anchor works → confirm Sidebar still shows the extraction in "This document" context section → upload a NON-requirements doc → confirm UserStoriesSection doesn't render).
- **2026-05-01 · M14.1.a** Backend lens architecture + dossier schema + master prompt. **Why**: M14 pivots Lucid to a generic doc-understanding tool whose primary output is a 4-act narrated dossier (Orient → Structure → Interrogate → Act). This commit lands the foundation — schema, prompt, dispatcher — without any user-visible change yet (frontend dispatcher comes in M14.1.b). **DB schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py), [db/session.py](backend/db/session.py)): new `lens VARCHAR DEFAULT 'stories'` + `lens_payload JSON` columns on `Extraction` via the existing soft-migration pattern. Existing rows stay `lens='stories'`; new dossier rows write the full DocumentDossier JSON to `lens_payload` and leave the brief/actors/stories/nfrs/gaps columns mostly empty (with the carve-out below). **Lens registry** ([services/lenses/](backend/services/lenses/)): new `stories.py` (thin wrapper around existing `extract_requirements` for back-compat) + `dossier.py` (the new master schema + prompt + extractor) + `__init__.py` (the `LENSES` dict + `normalize()` helper that defaults unknown values to `'dossier'`). **DocumentDossier schema** ([services/lenses/dossier.py](backend/services/lenses/dossier.py)): 14 nested Pydantic models defining the full 4-act dossier — `Brief`, `TLDRLadder`, `FiveW1H`, `GlossaryTerm`, `Mindmap` (with explicit 3-level nesting cap via `MindmapBranch` → `MindmapSubBranch` → `MindmapLeaf` instead of unbounded recursion), `DomainBreakdown` (7 fixed lenses — Business Purpose, Stakeholders, Process Flow, Data, Rules, Metrics, Problems-Opportunities), `SystemsView` (entities + flows + feedback loops), `WhyStep`, `Assumption` (with risk_level), `FailureMode`, `ProbingQuestion` (with why_it_matters), `ActionItem` (owner + when + source quote), `RevisitItem`, `UserStory` (folded in per M14 pick (b)). Top-level `DocumentDossier` adds the narrative scaffolding — `overture` paragraph, `act_intro` per chapter, `bridge_*_to_*` strings between every section, `closing` line. **Master prompt** (in same file): instructs Claude to produce the 4-act arc, write per-doc bridges (not generic transitions), open with a hook-with-tease, close with a one-line action that pays off the tease, ground every claim in source quotes, and adapt tone to doc type (research paper vs vendor proposal vs meeting transcript). 5 Whys must be exactly 5; mindmap caps at 3 levels; user_stories only populated for requirements-shaped docs. **Dispatcher** ([services/extractions.py](backend/services/extractions.py)): `call_claude` gains `lens` kwarg (default 'stories' at Python layer for back-compat), branches to `extract_dossier` or `extract_requirements`. New `persist_dossier_extraction` writes the dossier row — `lens='dossier'`, full JSON in `lens_payload`, `brief` mirrored from `dossier.brief`, `stories` mirrored from `dossier.user_stories` (so any back-compat reader of `extraction.stories` keeps working when the dossier identifies user stories), other stories-shape columns empty. `extraction_to_record` now surfaces `lens` + `lens_payload` on every API response. **Route** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): `/api/extract` accepts `lens` form param (default 'dossier' via `normalize()` for new uploads — frontend will pass it explicitly in M14.1.b). The existing rerun route in `routers/extractions.py` is untouched and stays on the stories path for now (M14.1.c will port it). **Mock dossier** for no-API-key paths so the UI renders end-to-end without Claude calls. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest. End-to-end script (mock dossier → call_claude(lens='dossier') → persist_dossier_extraction → extraction_to_record) round-trips lens + lens_payload correctly. Stories back-compat verified independently — existing extract → persist → record path still produces lens='stories', lens_payload=None, stories count=3 as before. **What's next**: M14.1.b frontend dispatch + DossierPane skeleton; M14.1.c sticky nav + streaming integration. **Not browser-verified**.
- **2026-05-01 · M14.0** Rebrand to **Lucid**. **Why**: M14 pivots the product from "BRD → user stories" (one-trick PM tool) to "any document → narrated dossier" (workspace for document understanding). "StoryForge" no longer matches the scope; "Lucid" was picked over Mindforge / Grasp / Margin for its two-syllable AI-native feel and natural pairing with the new tagline. **Tagline**: "Understand any document" (was "Requirements → User Stories"). **What changed**: every user-facing surface — browser tab title, package.json name, Landing hero (headline shifted from "Turn messy docs into shippable stories" to "Understand any document"; subhead generalized from BRD/PM-flavoured to any doc type; HowItWorks step #2 retitled "Watch Lucid read it" with new dossier-flavoured body; testimonial + FAQ + footer copy; brand mark in Nav), SignIn brand mark + explainer (rewritten to describe the dossier capability), SignUp brand mark + comment, Sidebar brand row, ShareView (3 mentions), Settings (managed-mode banner + integrations description + email feedback subject), PushToNotionModal copy, api.js export filename (`storyforge-export.zip` → `lucid-export.zip`), e2e public spec text matcher. **What stays "storyforge"** (intentionally): env vars (`STORYFORGE_MASTER_KEY`, `STORYFORGE_BYOK_MODE`, `STORYFORGE_MODEL`, `STORYFORGE_DB`, `STORYFORGE_API_RATE_LIMIT_PER_MINUTE` — renaming would require coordinated Render dashboard updates and risks breaking production decryption), DB table names, Python module logger names (`storyforge.byok` etc), localStorage keys (`storyforge:theme`, `storyforge:studio:sourceRatio`, `storyforge:extractions` — renaming would wipe user theme + extraction history on next reload). All "internal-StoryForge / external-Lucid" decisions documented in styles.css comment header so future maintainers know it's deliberate. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (sign out → / → confirm "Lucid" + new headline → /sign-in → confirm bulb explainer mentions Lucid → /sign-up → confirm brand mark → sign in → confirm sidebar reads Lucid → open extraction → push to Notion modal → confirm copy reads "Lucid integration"). Internal cleanup of env-var / module names is M14-deferred — only ship if needed.

- **2026-05-01 · M13.4** Brand swap purple → mint/teal. **Why**: user wanted "light green based" palette to give freshness in place of the original indigo-500 brand. Picked teal-500 (`#14b8a6`) over emerald or sage because (a) it's distinct from `--success: #10b981` (emerald) so success badges still read as semantically distinct, (b) it's the modern AI/SaaS palette (Linear, Vercel, Stripe-docs use the same family), (c) it pairs naturally with cyan + sky for the hero gradient (teal → cyan → sky reads as "fresh + clean + capable"). **Variable swap** ([styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)): light theme `--accent` indigo-500 → teal-500, `--accent-strong` indigo-600 → teal-600, `--accent-soft` indigo-50 → teal-50, `--accent-ink` indigo-700 → teal-700. Dark theme equivalents bumped to teal-400 / 500 / 900 / 200 (lighter brand for dark surfaces, deep teal-900 for chip backgrounds, teal-200 for ink-on-soft text). `--border-focus` + `--shadow-focus` retuned to the teal alpha. Hero gradients (`--gradient`, `--gradient-hero`, `--gradient-soft`, dark variant) all swapped from indigo → purple → pink to teal → cyan → sky. **Hardcoded swaps**: Landing.jsx Logo brand-badge gradient, "Most popular" pricing badge gradient, ProductPreview ArtifactCard accent tone (`#a5b4fc` → `#5eead4` for the bg/fg pair), pricing card highlighted shadow color all flipped to teal. Landing CSS `--lp-accent-1` (was indigo alpha) → teal-500 alpha; `--lp-accent-2` (was purple alpha) → cyan-500 alpha. Light + dark Landing variants both updated. Favicon SVG gradient stops + `<meta name="theme-color">` flipped to teal-600 (`#0d9488`). Logo component (in icons.jsx) gradient stops swapped. **What stays purple**: the `--purple` named utility tone (`#9333ea`) + matching `--purple-soft`/`--purple-ink` are kept for Badge variety — used as a *tone* (alongside accent/success/warn/danger/info/pink), not as the brand. Same for `--pink`. **Trade-offs**: every Badge/IconTile that uses `tone="accent"` (~15 component sites in EmptyState, ArtifactsPane, App.jsx) automatically picks up teal because they consume the CSS vars — no per-component edit needed. The teal-cyan-sky gradient feels noticeably cooler than the indigo-purple-pink it replaces; if a warmer/calmer alternative is preferred (sage `#84a98c` or muted lime `#65a30d`) the swap is the same 8-var edit. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (sign in → confirm sidebar active-pill / IconTile "Sparkles" / Badge "Live" colors all read as teal not indigo → open Models/Settings → confirm Section icons + IconTiles teal → /sign-out → /sign-in → confirm bulb yellow stays yellow + page background lit-state still warm-cream → / signed-out → confirm Landing hero gradient is teal-cyan, "Most popular" badge teal, ArtifactCard accent tone teal — toggle OS dark mode → confirm dark variant teal accents pop against dark surface).

- **2026-05-01 · M13.2.c** SignInPage polish — six fixes from a screenshot review of the lit state. **Why**: M13.2 + M13.2.b shipped the bulb mechanic but a wide-viewport screenshot exposed (a) a mysterious rectangular yellow cage framing the bulb after pull, (b) bulb too small for the page real estate (~90px in a 1500px viewport — read as "icon" not "hero"), (c) glow halo too tight (only ~40px past the bulb edge — couldn't sell the "lights up the room" metaphor), (d) "StoryForge" title visually disconnected from the bulb (24px gap), (e) form anchored hard right against page edge (~600-800px of empty horizontal space), (f) cord+bulb felt static once lit. **Fix 1 — diagnose the cage** ([SignInPage.jsx](frontend/src/pages/SignInPage.jsx), [styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)): root cause was `.bulb-cord-btn:focus-visible { outline: 2px solid #fbbf24 }` — the outline drew around the entire `<button>` bounds (cord 180px + bulb 130px ~= 310px tall), painting a yellow rectangular cage every time the button held focus. Moved the focus ring from the button to `.bulb-cord-btn:focus-visible .bulb-svg-wrap` with `outline-offset: 12px` + `border-radius: 50%` — keyboard users now see a tight round halo around the bulb, not a cage. Also added `e.currentTarget.blur()` inside the `pull` handler so even sighted-mouse users don't see a lingering focus state on the cord post-pull. **Fix 2 — bulb size**: SVG render dimensions bumped 90×130 → 150×216 (viewBox unchanged, path scales). Bulb now reads as the page's hero element. **Fix 3 — cord length**: 180px → 140px (the bigger bulb wanted less cord — total visual weight stays similar). **Fix 4 — halo bloom**: `.bulb-halo` inset extended from `-120px` to `-280px` (560px wide bloom area), centre alpha bumped 0.55 → 0.75, added a 35% mid-stop at 0.20 for a smoother gradient. The bulb now visibly illuminates the surrounding page area when lit. **Fix 5 — column layout**: was `grid-template-columns: minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 1fr)` (50/50 split, anything-goes width). New: `minmax(360px, 520px) minmax(360px, 480px)` + `justify-content: center`. Total grid ~1000px max, centered horizontally on the page — bulb and form sit close to page-center with even outer margins, instead of pinned to opposite edges. **Fix 6 — pendulum sway**: new `@keyframes bulb-sway { 0%,100% { transform: rotate(-1.2deg) } 50% { transform: rotate(1.2deg) } }` runs on `.bulbpage.is-lit .bulb-cord-btn:not(.is-tugging)` for 4.2s ease-in-out infinite. The whole rig swings around the cord's top-center anchor like a real pendant lamp. Excluded while `is-tugging` so the spring-back doesn't conflict; killed under `prefers-reduced-motion`. **Fix 7 — title gap**: `.bulb-explainer` margin-top inline-overridden 24 → 8px; `<h1>` `marginTop: 12` removed. Title now sits right under the bulb's halo, picks up the warm tone via the page background gradient. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (sign out → /sign-in → confirm bulb hangs centered-left, big and crisp → pull cord → confirm no rectangular cage, glow blooms wide across the left half, page genuinely warms, form fades in centered-right, bulb gently sways → keyboard: Tab to cord → confirm round focus halo around bulb only → toggle OS Reduce Motion → confirm sway disabled, instant lit).

- **2026-05-01 · M13.2** Bulb-and-cord SignInPage — interactive sign-in surface that doubles as a brand moment. **Why**: the previous SignInPage (M10.2) was a polished but generic "logo + form on a gradient" — fine but forgettable. The brief was to make the page itself the hook: dim room + bulb on a cord, click the cord to "turn on the lights" and reveal the form. Skeuomorphic, playful, signals "this isn't a clone of Clerk's defaults". **Mechanics** ([SignInPage.jsx](frontend/src/pages/SignInPage.jsx)): two pieces of state — `lit` (bulb status) + `tugging` (cord-snap-back flag, lasts 250ms). Click on the cord button: tug fires immediately for the spring-back animation, `lit` flips ~200ms later so the bulb glow chases the cord motion (feels causal). Bulb drawn inline as SVG: round-tapered glass envelope, two-loop filament, three-ridge screw cap. **Animation** ([styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css), new `.bulbpage` block): page background transitions from `linear-gradient(#08080b → #14141d)` (off, dim) to `radial-gradient(circle at 50% 22%, #fef3c7 0%, #fafaf9 35%)` (on, warm cream — bulb is the light source, page brightens around it). Bulb glass fills `#fde68a`, filament becomes `#b45309`, halo (radial gradient inset -120px around bulb) fades from `opacity 0` to `1`. Cord-tug uses a cubic-bezier(.34, 1.56, .64, 1) spring. Clerk widget gates on `.bulbpage.is-lit` — opacity 0 + translateY(16px) → opacity 1 + 0, with a 350ms delay so the bulb glow registers first. **Accessibility**: cord is a `<button>` (not a div) — keyboard focus + Space/Enter activate the same handler as click. Focus-visible outline (yellow, matches the lit colour). `prefers-reduced-motion` media query strips every transition + animation in one block. Clerk widget stays in the DOM throughout (only opacity gates it visually) so screen readers can still tab to it pre-pull. **Skip path**: "turn on the light" text link at page bottom triggers the same `pull()` handler — for users who don't want to play the metaphor; sits next to "Create an account" → /sign-up so the bottom row covers both off-ramps. **Trade-off**: explicit one-click friction before the form. Mitigated by the skip link and the reduced-motion path. Hint copy ("↑ Pull the cord to sign in") gently bounces above the bulb to telegraph the affordance — disappears once lit. Sign-up page is unchanged for this milestone (could mirror the bulb pattern as M13.2.b if user likes it). **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (visit /sign-in signed-out → confirm dim page with bulb + explainer + bouncing pull hint → click cord → cord snaps + bulb glows + page warms + Clerk widget fades in below → sign in → / loads the studio → also verify the skip link below page works → also verify keyboard: Tab to cord → Space → same effect → also try OS Reduce Motion → confirm instant lit).
- **2026-05-01 · M13.1.2** Landing page expanded with ProductPreview / Testimonials / Pricing / FAQ + light-theme variant. **Why**: M13.1.1 landed the hero shell; visitors had nothing below the fold to convert on. Modern B2B landings need price transparency + objection handling (FAQ) + at least one trust signal (testimonials, even placeholder) before the second CTA. **New sections**: (1) **ProductPreview** ([Landing.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Landing.jsx)) — 3 mock artifact cards (story / gap / NFR) demonstrating the source-quote provenance pattern with monospace ID tags + tonal pills + italic blockquote; positioned right after hero so the visitor sees the actual output before reading copy about it. (4) **FAQ** — 6 collapsible `<details>` Q&As: doc types, BYOK vs managed, accuracy, privacy, push integrations, cancellation. Native HTML disclosure (no JS state). **Light theme variant**: colours moved to CSS vars on a new `.landing-root` selector in [styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css); `@media (prefers-color-scheme: light)` block flips them to a light palette (warm-white bg, dark text, dark-pill CTAs). Scoped under `.landing-root` so they don't leak into the in-app theme system. No JS toggle — signed-out visitors don't load theme settings, so OS preference is the right hint. **Copy + structure**: headline tightened to "Turn messy docs into shippable stories." (was "Turn messy requirements into clear user stories" — punchier, more action-focused). Subhead reordered. Section order finalised: hero → preview → how-it-works → testimonials → pricing → FAQ → footer (standard B2B SaaS funnel: hook → show → explain → trust → price → objections → close). Anchor nav added: top-right Pricing + FAQ links jump to #pricing / #faq. Reusable `<SectionHeader eyebrow title sub>`, `<CtaPrimary>`, `<CtaGhost>` primitives factored out. **Trade-offs**: testimonials are placeholders — flagged in code with a TODO. Pricing values are duplicated between landing copy and `services/plans.py`; could fetch via a `/api/plans` route but marketing copy changes once a quarter so a lift-and-edit on plan changes is fine. FAQ uses native `<details>` instead of a custom accordion — 0 JS, semantic HTML, but no animated chevron. - **2026-04-26 · M3.4.6 — closes M3.4** Managed-key path behind `STORYFORGE_BYOK_MODE` env var. Three deployment shapes one env var picks between, no schema or wire-protocol change. **Modes** (defined in [services/byok.py](backend/services/byok.py)): `strict` (default, the existing behaviour — user must BYOK; server's `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is NOT used for extractions, so missing user key drops to mock mode), `managed` (server pays — every extraction uses the server env key, user-stored keys are ignored, BYOK form is hidden in the UI), `choice` (user can BYOK or fall back to server env — header > stored > env precedence). New `byok_mode()` helper validates the env value (unknown values fall back to strict + a warning log). **Resolver rewrite** ([services/byok.py](backend/services/byok.py)): `resolve_user_byok` is now mode-aware — picks header/stored/env per mode rather than the previous "always honour stored, no env fallback" path. The model_default lookup is mode-independent. **extract.py simplified** ([extract.py](backend/extract.py)): the in-extract `effective_key = api_key or os.environ.get(...)` fallback is gone — the resolver is now authoritative. This is the WHOLE POINT of strict mode: it prevents the server env key from leaking into live extractions when the user hasn't BYOK'd. **Surface** ([backend/models.py](backend/models.py)): new `byok_mode: str` field on `UserSettingsRead` — populated in [routers/me.py](backend/routers/me.py)`._to_read` so the frontend gets the server-wide setting alongside the per-user payload (one round-trip, no second endpoint). **UI** ([frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): `ApiKeyForm` accepts a `byokMode` prop. In `managed` mode the entire form is replaced with a "Managed mode — extractions use the StoryForge-hosted Anthropic key" banner so users don't store a key that will be ignored. In `choice` mode the inactive-state copy switches to "extractions use the server-managed key. Add your own to bring your own billing." In `strict` mode (default), copy reads "extractions run in mock mode until you add a key." Model picker stays usable in all modes since `model_default` is meaningful regardless of who pays for the call. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. End-to-end resolver matrix run against a temp SQLite + seeded UserSettings — all 9 cells (3 modes × 3 user states: no-stored / stored / header-override) returned the expected key. **Smoke envar**: `STORYFORGE_BYOK_MODE=managed` documented in `.env.example`. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (set env to `managed`, restart backend, open /models → confirm BYOK form replaced by managed banner, model picker still works → set env to `choice` → confirm form shows with "optional" copy → run extraction without saving a key → confirm Live mode on completion).
- **2026-04-26 · Bundle code-split** Initial JS chunk dropped from 603 KB → 191 KB (~68% smaller, 165 KB → 53 KB gzipped) by splitting vendor halves out and lazy-loading every off-home route + every push modal. **Vite config** ([vite.config.js](frontend/vite.config.js)): `build.rollupOptions.output.manualChunks` carves `react-vendor` (react / react-dom / react-router-dom — 178 KB / 58 KB gz) and `clerk` (96 KB / 26 KB gz) into their own files so they hash and cache independently of app code. (Tried adding `@sentry/react` to the manualChunks map but tree-shaking already dropped Sentry to a 36-byte re-export stub — DSN-gated init in `lib/sentry.js` makes the heavy SDK dead code in dev/preview builds; chunk removed to avoid the empty file.) **App.jsx** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): every off-home route swapped to `React.lazy()` — Account, Documents, Project, Settings (which exports four named pages — ModelsPage / ToolsPage / IntegrationsPage / SupportPage — all in one shared chunk), CompareView, ShareView, SignInPage, SignUpPage. Each push modal (Jira / Linear / GitHub / Slack / Notion) + SaveExampleModal lazy too — they're conditional already, so the chunks only fetch when the user opens one. New `<RouteFallback>` component renders a centred Spinner inside the Suspense fallback so the page doesn't collapse to zero height during the chunk swap; modals fall back to `null` because the button-press feedback covers the brief gap. Both `<Routes>` blocks (the inner studio router and the top-level auth gate) wrapped in Suspense. **Trade-offs**: home / studio route stays eager because it's the first page everyone hits — splitting it would add a Suspense flash on cold load. SourcePane / ArtifactsPane / GapsRail / Sidebar / TopBar all live with the studio for the same reason. Per-modal Suspense rather than one shared boundary so an open modal doesn't block another from opening if a chunk fetch is slow. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean (no more 500 KB warning; 19 chunks total). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open `/` → confirm studio renders without flash → click Documents → brief spinner → Documents loads → open a push modal → confirm it appears within ~150 ms even on slow 3G).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.5.3.b** Backend unread-comment tracking — replaces the M4.5.3 localStorage with a per-(user, extraction) row so the badge follows the user across devices/browsers/profiles. **New table** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): `ExtractionView(user_id, extraction_id, last_seen_at)` — composite PK (user_id, extraction_id). FK to `extraction.id` so views vanish if the extraction is deleted. Soft-migrated by SQLModel's `create_all`. **Service helpers** ([services/extractions.py](backend/services/extractions.py)): `count_unread_comments(session, extraction_id, user_id)` returns 0 when there's no view row yet (first-visit semantics — prevents the badge from screaming on a freshly-imported extraction with 47 historical comments); when there is, counts comments whose `created_at > view.last_seen_at`. `mark_extraction_seen(session, extraction_id, user_id)` upserts the view row to `now()`. `extraction_to_record` gains optional `session=` + `user_id=` kwargs — when both are provided it computes `unread_comment_count`; when not, defaults to 0. Made optional so the existing PATCH/regen/rerun/import callsites (where unread=0 is correct anyway) didn't all need touching. **Schema** ([backend/models.py](backend/models.py)): `ExtractionRecord.unread_comment_count: int = 0` — flows to the frontend on every GET /api/extractions/{id}. **Routes** ([routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py)): GET passes `session` + `user.user_id` through to `extraction_to_record`. New `POST /api/extractions/{id}/seen` returns 204 — wraps `mark_extraction_seen`. **Frontend swap** ([frontend/src/api.js](frontend/src/api.js), [frontend/src/App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): `lib/extraction_seen.js` deleted entirely (was localStorage). New `markExtractionSeenApi(id)` calls the new POST. App.jsx unread state now seeds from `extraction.unread_comment_count` on every extraction fetch; `markExtractionSeen` callback hits the new endpoint optimistically (sets local to 0 immediately, soft-fails on POST). New comments posted in-session by *other* users bump unread locally so the badge appears before the next refetch — comments by the current user stay at 0 (those are by definition already-seen). **Trade-offs**: counted at read time rather than maintained as a denormalized counter — keeps things simple and correct, single small query per GET. Could shard or cache if extraction GETs ever become hot. The Sidebar prop interface (`unread`, `onMarkSeen`) is unchanged — the swap is invisible to SidebarExtractionSection. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean (still 580 KB chunk — bundle code-split is the next task). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open extraction with 5+ comments from another user → confirm badge shows N → click "N new" pill in sidebar → badge clears → reload → confirm still 0 → switch browser/device, sign in, open same extraction → confirm 0 unread carries across).
- **2026-04-27 · M11.1** Documents — multi-select + bulk actions. **Why**: bulk delete and bulk-move-to-project required N round-trips to the API, one row at a time, before this — high friction for users with >5 documents to triage. Search (debounced backend `q` param + visible search bar) was already shipped pre-M11; M11 adds the missing batch-action layer. **Selection** ([Documents.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Documents.jsx)): new `selected: Set<id>` state. Each row gets a 16px checkbox to the left of the IconTile; CSS-driven (`.row-checkbox` in [styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)) so it's hidden by default and revealed on row hover OR forced visible inline when any row is selected (the user is mid-pick). Selected rows visually distinct: accent-soft background + accent border. Click semantics swap when a selection is active — clicking the row toggles selection (Linear-style); clearing the selection restores click-to-open. **Bulk-action header**: when `hasSelection`, the page heading swaps for an accent-soft strip showing `[checkbox] N selected · [Select all N] · Move to project · Delete · Clear`. The Move-to-project button reuses the existing `<MoveMenu>` dropdown — same project-picker UX as the per-row variant. **Bulk delete**: serial deletes (one failure doesn't strand the batch); per-failure count surfaces in the final toast ("Deleted 7, 1 failed"). No undo for bulk — refactoring the single-row undo (refetches the full payload pre-delete) into N parallel pre-fetches felt like overkill for an explicit "Are you sure?" confirmation. **Bulk move**: same serial pattern; works for both moving to a project and removing from one (`projectId === null`). PostHog events not added — leaving for the next analytics audit. **Trade-offs**: range-select with shift-click deferred — can ship as M11.b once the basic batch flow has user feedback. The bulk-action header overlay sits in the same place as the regular heading rather than an overlay/floating bar — keeps the layout simple but means the search bar reflows; acceptable since users typing in search aren't usually mid-bulk-action. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open Documents → hover a row to confirm checkbox reveal → check 2-3 boxes → confirm header swaps → click Move to project, pick one → confirm rows update + toast → check 5+ → click Delete → confirm count in confirm dialog).

- **2026-04-27 · M10.1** Design tokens — surface scale + motion + spacing + brand gradient. **Additive layer** over the existing `--bg`/`--text`/`--accent` system; nothing visual changes yet, M10.2 + M10.3 build on these. **Surface scale** ([styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)): `--surface-0` (page) → `--surface-1` (cards) → `--surface-2` (popovers) → `--surface-3` (active). - **2026-04-27 · M8.6 — closes M8** Studio reshuffle, sub-step 6 — narrow-viewport collapse. **Why**: the wide-viewport three-pane layout (source + artifacts + optional gaps rail) breaks below ~900px — panes get squeezed below readable widths and the resize handle becomes useless. - **2026-04-27 · M8.5** Studio reshuffle, sub-step 5 — multi-doc tab strip in SourcePane. **Why**: pre-M8.5 the `===== DOC N: name =====` markers (M7.5) rendered as plain paragraphs in the source body — visible noise. Plus there was no fast way to jump between docs in a multi-doc extraction; users had to scroll through everything. **New helper** ([lib/multi_doc.js::splitParagraphsByDoc](frontend/src/lib/multi_doc.js)): walks the raw_text, returns `{ docs: [{idx, name}], paragraphs: [{docIdx, text}] }`. Marker paragraphs are stripped (they're now tabs, not text); every surviving paragraph carries the docIdx of the marker that preceded it. Single-doc inputs return `docs: []` so the tab strip stays hidden — clean back-compat. **SourcePane** ([components/SourcePane.jsx](frontend/src/components/SourcePane.jsx)): rewrote the body render to consume `splitParagraphsByDoc` instead of the old paragraph-only split. The first paragraph of each doc gets a `data-doc-anchor={idx}` attribute so the click handler + scroll-spy can target it. Tab strip renders below the header pills (one pill per doc, FileText icon + name, active state in solid accent + white). Click → smooth-scroll to that doc's first paragraph + immediately set active tab. Scroll-spy via IntersectionObserver — when a doc anchor enters the [-20%, -60%] vertical band of the body's viewport, that doc becomes active; the topmost-visible anchor wins so multi-doc-visible cases pick the natural reading head. **Removed**: SourcePane's per-doc download list (the M7.5.b `<Button>` chain in the header). The Sidebar's "This document → Sources" section (M8.1) already hosts these, and one source of truth beats two parallel surfaces. Single source-pane downloads (the legacy "Download original" button for single-doc rows) also removed for symmetry — Sidebar handles the single-source case too. **Imports cleaned**: dropped `parseDocNames` (replaced by `splitParagraphsByDoc`), `downloadExtractionSourceApi`, `useToast`, `Button`, `Download` icon. **Trade-off**: tab strip is rendered inside the (currently-non-sticky) header — when the source body scrolls, the tab strip scrolls out of view too. Could make it sticky (`position: sticky` on a separate wrapper above the body); deferred since the typical multi-doc use is "click tab → read doc → maybe click another tab" rather than constant tab visibility. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean (158.15 KB gzipped, +0.4 KB from M8.4 — net of removed download UI offset by the tab strip + scroll-spy logic). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open a multi-doc extraction → confirm tab strip appears with one tab per doc → click tabs to confirm scroll → scroll the body to confirm active tab updates → confirm marker text no longer appears as paragraphs).
- **2026-04-27 · M8.4** Studio reshuffle, sub-step 4 — comments anchoring polish. **Why**: the existing trigger ([Comments.jsx::CommentThread](frontend/src/components/Comments.jsx)) was a bare 13px MessageSquare icon that changed color (accent-strong) when comments existed but otherwise looked like a stray glyph. Easy to miss as both a "thread exists" signal and as a "you can comment here" affordance. **Change**: when `comments.length > 0` the trigger renders as a soft accent pill (`accent-soft` background, accent-ink text, pill radius, padded) with the count + the word "comment(s)" so it scans as a real piece of UI content; on hover it fills with the solid accent + white text. When empty, the trigger stays quiet (bare icon + transparent background) but gains a `bg-hover` on hover so first-time users notice it as clickable. **Both anchor sites benefit without per-site changes**: ArtifactsPane already uses `<CommentThread>` in two places (the Brief section header's `action` slot and inside each story card's header row alongside DocBadge); the change is contained inside CommentThread's button styling. - **2026-04-27 · M8.2** Studio reshuffle, sub-step 2 — resizable source/artifacts split. **New component** ([ResizeHandle.jsx](frontend/src/components/ResizeHandle.jsx)): a 4px-wide vertical separator between two flex children. Owns the drag math (clientX → ratio of containerRef's bounding rect) and emits `onChange(ratio)` on every move; the parent owns the persisted value + the `min`/`max` clamps so the handle stays a dumb coordinate emitter. Pointer events (mouse/pen/touch) with `setPointerCapture` so a fast drag doesn't drop events when the cursor crosses out of the 4px stripe. Hit area widened to 8px via padding + negative margin so the user doesn't have to pixel-hunt. `touch-action: none` keeps mobile from interpreting the drag as a scroll. `document.body.style.userSelect = 'none'` during drag so text doesn't highlight. **State + persistence** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): new `sourceRatio` state hydrated from localStorage `storyforge:studio:sourceRatio` (default `0.42` = current width). Clamped to `[0.20, 0.70]` so neither pane can be hidden. Written back on every drag tick — `setItem` is cheap and a one-tick stale write on refresh is fine. New `studioBodyRef` on the `.body` div feeds the handle's bounding-rect math. **Pane** ([SourcePane.jsx](frontend/src/components/SourcePane.jsx)): hardcoded `width: '42%'` becomes `width` prop (default `'42%'` for back-compat). Added `flexShrink: 0` defensively so percent width is respected when total content might press at the container edge. The existing `minWidth: 340` stays as the hard floor below which the source paragraphs become unreadable. **Trade-off**: ratio applies whether or not the GapsRail is open — when GapsRail is mounted (320px on the right of `<main>`), the source/artifacts split happens inside the leftover space, so a 42% source pane is 42% of (viewport − sidebar 248px − GapsRail 320px). Reasonable. Could revisit if the relative widths feel wrong with both panels expanded. ArtifactsPane unchanged (still `flex: 1` — fills whatever the source pane leaves). **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean (157.60 KB gzipped, +0.5 KB). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drag the handle left/right → confirm the panes resize smoothly; refresh the page → confirm the ratio sticks; try below 20% / above 70% → confirm it clamps; on touch device → confirm drag works without page scroll).
- **2026-04-27 · M8.1** Studio reshuffle, sub-step 1 — "This document" contextual section in the app Sidebar. **Why**: TopBar had grown to 7+ buttons (theme · gaps toggle · re-run · new · share · push · save-as-example · export · version picker) and the version picker + gaps toggle weren't actually TopBar-shaped; they're document navigation, which belongs in the left rail. **New component** ([SidebarExtractionSection.jsx](frontend/src/components/SidebarExtractionSection.jsx)): renders only when an extraction is open. Layout: filename row + version chip; collapsible Versions list (when N > 1) with the same per-row "Compare" link the TopBar used to host (preserves the M7.6 routing convention, `idA = older` / `idB = newer`); collapsible Sources list (multi-doc only — wraps `downloadExtractionSourceApi` with `parseDocNames` for friendly per-doc names, replacing the same buttons in SourcePane's header); a stats row with a clickable gaps badge (toggles `showGaps` — same handler the TopBar IconButton used) and a comment count Badge. **Sidebar** ([Sidebar.jsx](frontend/src/components/Sidebar.jsx)): gains `extractionContext` prop. When non-null, renders `<SidebarExtractionSection {...extractionContext} />` below the global nav (Documents / Projects / Account / Settings). When null, Sidebar is unchanged — homepage and other routes stay clean. **State lift** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): version-chain fetch was inside TopBar; lifted to App so Sidebar + (now-stripped) TopBar share one source of truth. New `versions` state + `useEffect` that re-fetches on `extractionId` change. App wires `extractionContext = extraction && isHome ? { extraction, versions, comments, showGaps, onSwitchVersion, onToggleGaps } : null` — `isHome` guard means the section disappears when the user navigates to /documents or /settings without losing the open extraction state. **TopBar** ([TopBar.jsx](frontend/src/components/TopBar.jsx)): `VersionPicker` + `fmtTime` removed (relocated, not deleted — they live in the new component). Gaps toggle IconButton removed. Local versions state + `listVersionsApi` fetch removed (now upstream). `useNavigate` + `Check` + `ChevronDown` imports removed. New `currentVersion` prop accepts the live label so the existing "Live · v3" Badge can render without re-fetching. **Trade-offs**: I kept ProjectsSection in the Sidebar above the new section (global nav first, document context after) instead of shuffling sections around — least disruption. Comment count is total comments, not unread; M4.5.3 (per-user `last_seen_at`) will refine to "unread" later. The Sources list is duplicated in SourcePane's header for now; M8.5 will promote that into a tab strip and the SourcePane copy can be removed. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + vite clean (157.06 KB gzipped JS, +4 KB from M6.2.d, all the new section + comment-count import). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open an extraction with multiple versions → confirm the Sidebar shows the version list and "Compare" link works → toggle the gaps badge → confirm GapsRail opens/closes).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.2.d — closes M6** Jira OAuth 3LO. **Env-var gated** ([services/jira_oauth.py](backend/services/jira_oauth.py)): `is_enabled()` checks for `JIRA_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` + `JIRA_OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` — without those the OAuth UI is hidden and the API-token path remains the only flow. Production deploy needs to register an Atlassian developer app at developer.atlassian.com/console/myapps with the scopes `read:jira-work write:jira-work read:jira-user offline_access` (offline_access is required for the refresh token). The redirect URI is `<your-app>/api/integrations/jira/oauth/callback` — must be listed in the Atlassian app's allow-list. **Service**: standard 3LO — `mint_state(user_id)` (in-process dict, 10-minute TTL, single-use, cheap sweep), `authorize_url(state, redirect_uri)`, `exchange_code(code, redirect_uri)`, `refresh_access_token(refresh_token)` (Atlassian rotates the refresh_token in some responses — caller persists whatever they sent), `get_accessible_resources(access_token)` (lists Jira sites the token can reach — first one wins by default; M6.2.d.b can offer a picker for users with multiple sites). `is_access_token_stale()` returns True when within 60s of expiry — used by the decrypt path to refresh proactively, saving the first call from a 401-then-retry. **JiraClient refactor** ([services/jira.py](backend/services/jira.py)): now supports both auth modes — API-token (existing `auth=(email, token)`) or OAuth (Bearer `access_token`). `site_url` is tracked separately because OAuth's `base_url` is the Atlassian proxy (`api.atlassian.com/ex/jira/{cloud_id}`) which doesn't render `/browse/{key}` issue links — the user-facing site URL persists alongside. **Storage**: zero schema migration. The OAuth-shape connection lives inside the existing `IntegrationConnection.config_json` with `auth_type: 'oauth'` discriminator + encrypted `access_token` + `refresh_token` + `cloud_id` + `site_url` + ISO `access_token_expires_at`. Existing API-token rows (no `auth_type`) keep working — `_decrypt_jira_config` branches on the discriminator. The OAuth decrypt path also auto-refreshes the access_token when stale and writes the new tokens back to the DB so the next call benefits from the fresh access_token (avoids burning one refresh per request). **Routes** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): `GET /api/integrations/jira/oauth/status` (server config flag — public-shape, no secrets); `POST /api/integrations/jira/oauth/start` (returns the authorize URL with a fresh CSRF state); `GET /api/integrations/jira/oauth/callback` (unauthed at the route layer because Atlassian's browser redirect arrives without an Authorization header — CSRF state binds it back to the user; lives on a separate `unauth_router` mounted in main.py without `_protected_deps`). All other Jira routes (list_projects, push_to_jira) now use a single `_jira_client_from_cfg(cfg)` factory that branches on auth mode. **UI** ([Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): JiraConnectionForm fetches `/oauth/status` alongside the connection. When OAuth is enabled, a "Connect with Atlassian" primary button renders above the API-token form with a soft "or use an API token" divider. Click → POST start → `window.location.href = authorize_url` → user consents in Atlassian's UI → Atlassian redirects to our callback → backend stores connection → callback redirects to `/settings?jira_oauth=connected` → frontend toasts "Jira connected via Atlassian" and strips the query string. The connected display shows the site_url + an "(OAuth)" placeholder where the email field would normally be (so users can tell which auth mode they're on). **Trade-offs**: in-memory CSRF state (single Render instance constraint same as M6.7.c rate limiter — swap to Redis if we scale out); first accessible site auto-picked (no multi-site picker in v1); browser hard-redirect rather than popup (popups break in stricter browsers and add another moving piece). **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + vite clean. **Not OAuth-verified** — needs an Atlassian dev app's CLIENT_ID/SECRET in Render env vars to actually exercise the full flow. With them set, recommend smoke (Settings → "Connect with Atlassian" → consent in Atlassian → confirm redirect lands on /settings with a connected state and a real Jira push works).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.5.b** Notion property mapping — route story fields into structured Notion columns instead of stuffing everything in the page body. **Backend** ([services/notion.py](backend/services/notion.py)): new `NotionClient.get_database_schema(database_id)` returns `[{name, type}]` for the picker. `create_page` accepts an `extra_properties` dict that's merged into the request's `properties` alongside the existing title. `_PROP_BUILDERS` is a tiny dispatch table from Notion property type → per-type payload builder — supports `rich_text`, `select`, `multi_select`, `url`. Other types (formula, relation, files, etc.) are filtered out client-side in the picker so users can't pick a target the backend won't write to. `_build_blocks(story, skip_fields=…)` skips fields that have been routed into properties to avoid duplication; fall-through still handles un-mapped fields the same way as before. **Push** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): `PushToNotionRequest` gains `property_map: dict[str, NotionPropertyMapping]` where `NotionPropertyMapping = {name, type}`. The route translates the Pydantic model into a plain dict for the service. "— body only —" is always the first option (legacy behaviour). Schema fetches are cached per database id so re-picking is free. PostHog `push_to_notion_started` + `_finished` carry `mapped_count`. **Trade-offs**: each story-field has a fixed compatible-types whitelist (e.g. Criteria → multi_select only) — keeps the picker small + the per-type write logic minimal. Empty values skip the property write entirely (so re-pushing won't clobber an existing page's column with blanks). Title remains the auto-generated `"<id>: <want>"` — making it user-mappable would force a re-think of the page-creation contract. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + vite clean. **Not Notion-verified** — recommend smoke (open a Notion DB with a "Status" select column → push and map Section → Status → confirm pages land with the section value in the Status column instead of the body).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.7.d** OpenAPI spec page at `/api-docs`. **App config** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): FastAPI initialised with `docs_url="/api-docs"` (Swagger UI moved off the default `/docs`), `redoc_url=None` (we don't need both — Swagger's "Try it out" + Authorize is what users want), and a description string that explains the two auth options and the rate-limit + RO-token caveats. The raw spec stays at `/openapi.json` (FastAPI default) so codegen tools find it via convention. **Custom OpenAPI generator**: declares a `BearerAuth` HTTP scheme in `components.securitySchemes`, then walks every path under `/api/` (excluding a small `PUBLIC_PATHS` allowlist for `/api/health`, `/api/share/{token}`, `/api/webhooks/lemonsqueezy`) and appends `[{"BearerAuth": []}]` to each operation's `security` list. Result: Swagger UI's Authorize button accepts a Bearer token, and protected endpoints render with the lock icon + automatically attach the token on "Try it out" calls. **Settings** ([pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): added a "Full reference + Try it out at /api-docs" line below the curl example in the API-tokens section, with bold guidance on clicking Authorize and pasting the token. **Trade-offs**: docs page is unauthenticated (the spec describes the public API; secrets only flow when the user pastes a Bearer token via the modal). FastAPI's auto-extracted security is dependency-driven — since we use a raw `Header(default=None)` in `current_user` (rather than `HTTPBearer`), the security has to be declared via the custom generator; the alternative (refactoring `current_user` to use `HTTPBearer`) would simplify this but would also change the auth contract for every protected route. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + vite clean; `app.openapi()` confirmed to declare BearerAuth and apply it to `/api/extractions/{id}` while leaving `/api/health` security-free. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (open `/api-docs` → click Authorize → paste a token → expand any GET endpoint → Try it out → confirm 200).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.7.c** Per-token rate limiting. **Service** ([services/rate_limit.py](backend/services/rate_limit.py)): fixed-window counter (60-second window, default 60 req/min) keyed by token id. Why fixed-window over sliding-window or true token-bucket: simplicity wins at this scale — we're protecting against runaway scripts ("for i in range(1_000_000): post()") and noisy CI loops, not implementing a fair-queueing SLA. Memory bounded by `_MAX_TRACKED=5000` with a stale-bucket sweep at insert time. Configurable via `STORYFORGE_API_RATE_LIMIT_PER_MINUTE` env var (set to 0 to disable — useful in tests). **Auth dep** ([auth/deps.py](backend/auth/deps.py)): `CurrentUser.token_id: str | None` populated only on the API-token branch (Clerk sessions stay None). New `enforce_token_rate_limit` dep is a no-op when `token_id is None`; otherwise calls `check_and_record(token_id)` and raises 429 with the precise wait-time and a `Retry-After` header on hit. **Wiring** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): inserted into `_protected_deps` between `enforce_token_scope` and `welcome_check` so every protected route benefits uniformly; the three explicit-deps routes (`/api/extract`, `/api/extract/stream`, `/api/test-key`) get the dep added to their `dependencies=[…]` list to keep the gate symmetric. **Trade-off**: in-process vs Redis — single-Render-instance deployment makes in-process the right call (no extra dep, zero round-trips). When (if) we scale out, the public `check_and_record(token_id) -> retry_after | None` shape stays the same; only the storage swaps. Plan-quota gates (M3.5, monthly extraction count) are unchanged and complementary — that quota is per-user across all credentials; this is a per-token burst guard. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest. **Not load-tested** — recommend smoke (set the env var to a low number like 5, hammer GET /api/extractions with a token, confirm the 6th request returns 429 + Retry-After).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.7.b** Read-only API token scope. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): `ApiToken.scope` VARCHAR added via soft migration with `DEFAULT 'rw'` so existing tokens keep full access (no breaking change). Scope is immutable on a token; rotate to a new token to change. **Auth dep** ([auth/deps.py](backend/auth/deps.py)): `CurrentUser` gains `token_scope: str = 'rw'`. The token-path branch in `current_user` stamps it from the row; the Clerk JWT branch always stamps `'rw'` (Clerk sessions are full r/w by definition — only API tokens can be read-only). New `enforce_token_scope(request, user)` dep returns 403 with a precise message ("This API token is read-only. Use a read/write token for non-GET requests.") when `user.token_scope == 'ro'` and the method is not GET/HEAD/OPTIONS. **Wiring** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): inserted into `_protected_deps` between `current_user` and `welcome_check` so it runs uniformly across every protected router (extractions / projects / me / comments / integrations / api-tokens / share / billing). The three routes that don't use the protected list (`/api/extract`, `/api/extract/stream`, `/api/test-key`) get `enforce_token_scope` added to their explicit `dependencies=[…]` list so the gate is symmetric. **Schemas** ([backend/models.py](backend/models.py)): `ApiTokenCreateRequest.scope: Literal['rw','ro'] = 'rw'`; `ApiTokenCreateResponse` + `ApiTokenRead` carry the scope so the UI can render badges. **Settings UI** ([Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): create form gains a 130px scope dropdown next to the name input; selecting 'Read-only' surfaces a hint line below the form explaining the constraint. Each token row shows a per-row scope badge ("Read-only" in info tone, "Read/write" in neutral) so users can tell tokens apart at a glance. **Trade-off**: scope is binary (rw/ro) rather than per-resource (e.g. "extractions:read", "tokens:write") — keeps the dep simple and the UX learnable; granular scopes can layer in M6.7.b.b without breaking the existing two-value column. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + vite clean. **Not curl-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → create a "ro" token → curl GET /api/extractions with it (200) → curl POST /api/extract with it (expect 403 with the read-only message)).

- **2026-04-26 · M6.4.b + M6.4.c** GitHub label picker + repo pagination (one commit; both touch `services/github.py`). **M6.4.b — labels** ([services/github.py](backend/services/github.py)): `GitHubClient.list_labels(owner, repo)` returns `[{name, color}]` for the picked repo; `create_issue` accepts a `labels: list[str]` param that flows straight into the issue payload (GitHub silently drops unknowns — no per-label validation round-trip needed). `push_extraction(..., labels=…)` applies the same labels to every story-issue. - **2026-04-26 · M6.2.c** Org-shared connections — applies to all 5 trackers (Jira / Linear / GitHub / Slack / Notion) in one cross-cutting refactor. **Schema**: zero changes — `IntegrationConnection`'s composite PK on `(scope, scope_id, kind)` already supported it; only the route layer needed wiring. **Resolver** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): new `_resolve_connection(session, user, kind)` returns `(row, scope_used)` — prefers the user's personal connection, falls back to the workspace's shared one when the caller has an active org context. Least-surprise rule: a user with both keeps the personal one as default (they set it up explicitly); a user without one inherits the workspace's. New `_get_connection_at(scope, scope_id, kind)` for explicit-scope writes; new `_validate_write_scope(user, scope)` enforces that 'org' writes have an active org context (returns 400 with a clear message otherwise). `_upsert_connection()` collapses the five inline upsert blocks (each tracker had the same shape) into one helper. **Schemas** ([backend/models.py](backend/models.py)): every `*ConnectionRead` gains `scope: Literal['user','org']` so the UI knows which scope it's looking at; every `*ConnectionWrite` gains `scope = 'user'` (default preserves old client behaviour). **Routes**: every PUT calls `_validate_write_scope(user, payload.scope)` then `_upsert_connection(...)`; every DELETE accepts `?scope=user|org` (default 'user'); every GET uses `_resolve_connection`. **API client** ([frontend/src/api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): all 5 delete helpers accept `{scope}` and append `?scope=…`. **Settings UI** ([Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): new `useConnectionScope(initialScope)` hook returns `{scope, picker, badge}`. Picker is a "Share with workspace **{orgName}**" checkbox (renders only when `useOrganization()` returns one — silent no-op for personal-context users so the M6.2.c addition is invisible to non-org users). Badge ("Personal" or "Workspace · {orgName}") shows above the connected-display block so users can tell at a glance which scope a saved connection lives at. Each form passes `scope` in the PUT body and `{scope: conn?.scope}` in the disconnect call so a personal disconnect can't delete the workspace-shared connection (and vice versa). **Trade-offs taken**: GET still returns one effective connection (the resolved one) rather than both — keeps the dropdown UX simple. A user who wants to manage both scopes independently has to switch Clerk org context to view/edit the org-scoped one (one Clerk org switch is one click; cleaner than dual forms in the same page). Org write permission is currently any-org-member; M6.2.c.b can gate to admin/owner role using the `org_role` already on `CurrentUser`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + vite clean. **Not workspace-verified** — recommend smoke (sign in to a Clerk org → connect Jira → check "Share with workspace" → confirm badge says "Workspace · …" → sign in as a different org member → confirm Jira shows up as already-connected with the same workspace badge).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.2.b** Jira sub-task per criterion — opt-in checkbox on the push modal that turns each acceptance criterion into a tickable sub-task linked to the parent story. **Backend** ([services/jira.py](backend/services/jira.py)): `JiraClient.create_issue` gains `parent_key: str | None` — when set, adds `fields.parent.key` (Jira's required shape for sub-tasks). Returns None when the project has no sub-task type configured (some company-managed projects strip them); `push_extraction` then surfaces a single soft-fail row explaining why and skips sub-tasks for the batch (parent stories still push). **Push loop**: per story, after the parent issue is created, iterate `criteria` and `create_issue(issue_type=subtask_type, parent_key=parent.key, summary=criterion[:255])`.
