- **2026-04-26 · M7.5.b — closes M7** Per-doc source persistence + multi-doc download UI. Closes the last deferred sub-item under M7. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): `Extraction.source_file_paths: list[str]` JSON column added via soft migration (`ALTER TABLE … ADD COLUMN source_file_paths JSON DEFAULT '[]'` — works on SQLite + Postgres). The legacy `source_file_path` single-string column stays — we mirror the first path into it on multi-doc rows so any old reader keeps working. **Read-side resolver** ([services/extractions.py](backend/services/extractions.py)): new `resolved_source_paths(row)` returns the multi-list when populated; falls back to wrapping the single legacy path; else `[]`. Centralised so every consumer (record serialise / source endpoint / GDPR export / delete cleanup) reads the same way. **Write path**: `persist_extraction()` accepts `source_file_paths: list[str] | None`; both `/api/extract` and `/api/extract/stream` switch from "upload only when N==1" to a list of (name, bytes) buffered until after Claude succeeds, then write every file via `save_upload(extraction_id, name, data)` and pass the resulting paths into `persist_extraction`. R2 keys stay `<extraction_id>/<safe_name>` so the path-traversal guard already in `save_upload` carries over. Failed Claude call → no uploads stranded (deferred-write order matters). **Endpoint** ([routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py)): kept `/source` as the back-compat single-file URL (returns the first path); added `GET /{id}/sources/{idx}` for explicit per-doc downloads. Both routes share the same `_serve_source_path()` helper that does R2-presign-redirect or local FileResponse. Multi-doc downloads use the per-doc filename derived from the stored path's basename so the user sees recognisable names; single-doc keeps the row's original `filename`. **GDPR export** ([routers/me.py](backend/routers/me.py)): switched from the single-path branch to a `for stored in resolved_source_paths(e)` loop so multi-doc rows export all N originals into the per-extraction folder. **Delete** ([services/extractions.py](backend/services/extractions.py)): `delete_extraction` cleans up every R2/local path on the row instead of just the legacy column. **Frontend** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js) + [SourcePane.jsx](frontend/src/components/SourcePane.jsx)): new `downloadExtractionSourceApi(id, idx, fallbackName)` blob-downloads the per-index source. SourcePane renders inline below the filename — single-doc shows one "Download original" button; multi-doc shows a vertical list with the per-doc display name (resolved via `parseDocNames(raw_text)` from M7.5.c so the "Originals · N" UI matches the DocBadges on stories/NFRs/gaps). The `source_file_paths` field is now exposed on `ExtractionRecord` ([backend/models.py](backend/models.py)) so the UI doesn't need a side-fetch. **Trade-offs**: per-doc filenames in multi-doc mode come from the on-disk safe_name (basename of the stored path), not the original `f.filename` — close enough for the download UX without persisting a separate display-name column. The first uploaded file is mirrored into the legacy `source_file_path` column for back-compat; we never use it for resolution but stale callers won't crash. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (453 modules, 153.07 KB gzipped JS — +2.2 KB from M7.2, the SourcePane downloads UI + the new API helper). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (upload 2-3 files in one extract → confirm SourcePane shows one Download per doc → click each → confirm the originals download with their per-doc names → delete the extraction → confirm R2 bucket no longer holds any of the N files).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.2 (M7.2.1; .b/.c deferred)** Few-shot examples — input → expected-output pairs prepended to the extraction prompt for in-context learning. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): new `FewShotExample` table — `(id, user_id, org_id reserved for M7.2.b, name, input_text, expected_payload JSON, enabled, created_at, updated_at)`. JSON storage means no migration on payload-shape changes. **Cap**: 3 enabled per user (each example adds ~3K-8K input tokens — three is the cost-quality sweet spot for our extraction prompt size). Disabled rows stay in the table for easy re-enable. **Service** ([services/few_shot.py](backend/services/few_shot.py)): `resolve_enabled_examples(session, user_id)` returns the active set oldest-first (stable order across edits). Two format helpers because the call sites need different message shapes: `as_parse_messages()` for `messages.parse` (assistant turn = pretty JSON string of expected_payload — that's what the parse path expects) and `as_tool_messages()` for tool-use streaming (assistant `tool_use` block carrying expected_payload as `input`, immediately followed by a synthetic `tool_result` user turn — Anthropic requires every `tool_use` to be paired with a `tool_result` before the next user turn). **Wiring**: applied in `extract.py` (non-streaming) and `services/streaming.py` (SSE) — both unpack the example list into prepended messages, then append the real user turn. **Regen skipped** (`services/regen.py`): regen tools are per-section (`emit_stories` / `emit_nfrs` / `emit_gaps`) but our examples are full-extraction shape — the schemas don't match. Documented as a non-feature; users who want examples + regen can chain extract → edit → save-example workflows. **Capture path** ([routers/me.py](backend/routers/me.py)): `POST /api/me/few-shot-examples/from-extraction` body `{extraction_id, name, enabled}` — pulls live raw_text + payload from the named extraction. Primary UX path; most users won't author the JSON by hand. Plus standard CRUD (list / create-by-hand / patch / delete) with cap enforcement on the activate transition. **TopBar "Save as example"** (visible whenever an extraction is open): opens [SaveExampleModal](frontend/src/components/SaveExampleModal.jsx) — name input + enabled toggle + Save. Backend captures the snapshot. **Settings · "Few-shot examples"** ([pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): list view with active/inactive badge + Disable/Enable + Delete. Header shows "currently N of 3 enabled" so users can budget. Hand-editing the JSON deferred to M7.2.c — JSON shape is structured enough that a textarea is more dangerous than useful. Re-capture (extract again, edit, Save) replaces. **Frontend client** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): `listFewShotExamplesApi`, `createFewShotExampleApi`, `captureFewShotFromExtractionApi`, `patchFewShotExampleApi`, `deleteFewShotExampleApi`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (456 modules, 150.9 KB JS — +1.4 KB from M7.5, all the new modal + Settings section + TopBar button). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc → edit it via M4.1 → click "Save as example" → name it → confirm Settings shows it active → extract a different doc → confirm output matches the example's style).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.5 (M7.5.1; .b/.c deferred)** Multi-doc extraction — upload N files in one shot, get one combined extraction. **Refactor first**: pulled the per-file logic (read + ext + max_bytes + parse + image-vision + OCR fallback + per-pre-pass usage_log) out of the inline route handlers into [services/ingest.py](backend/services/ingest.py) `ingest_file()`. Routes used to share ~80 lines of duplicated parse-and-pre-pass; now they each call the same async helper in a loop. Net code in main.py drops despite gaining multi-file support. **`combine_raw_texts(items)`**: joins per-doc `(name, raw_text)` tuples with `===== DOC i: name =====` markers; single-doc inputs collapse to bare `raw_text` (no markers — backward compatible). Synthesized `source_name` is `"first.pdf + N more"` for multi; the user can override via the existing `filename` form field. **Routes**: both `/api/extract` and `/api/extract/stream` switch the `file` parameter from `UploadFile` → `list[UploadFile] = File(default=None)`. FastAPI parses repeated `file` form fields into a list — single-file uploads (one `file` field) become a 1-element list, so legacy clients keep working without change. **Source-file persistence (R2/disk) skipped when N > 1** — multi-doc loses individual source preservation in v1; the combined raw_text holds everything for click-to-source (M5.2), and the user has the originals locally. **Frontend** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): new `buildExtractForm()` helper accepts `file` as a single File, an array of Files, or a FileList — appends one `file` field per file; both `extract()` + `extractStream()` use it. [components/EmptyState.jsx](frontend/src/components/EmptyState.jsx): `file` state replaced with `files: File[]`; new `addFiles()` appends + de-dupes by `(name, size)`; new `removeFile(idx)`; staged files render as a vertical list with a `+ Add another file` button + per-row remove. Drop-zone hint now mentions multi-doc support. `<input multiple>` enables OS-level multi-pick. **Trade-offs**: M7.5.b (per-doc R2 storage + multi-source download UI) deferred — single combined raw_text is enough for the extraction itself; preserving N originals adds DB schema (`Extraction.source_file_paths: list`) and routing complexity for marginal value. M7.5.c (per-doc provenance on artifacts — "this story came from doc 2") would need extractor prompt changes to populate a new field; defer. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (455 modules, 149.5 KB JS — +0.3 KB from M7.4, all the new staging UI). Backend cov 54% baseline unchanged. **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (drag 2-3 files into the upload zone → confirm staging list shows all + Add Another works → click Extract → confirm one extraction with stories that draw from all docs + check `/api/me/usage` shows the right number of vision/ocr rows).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.4 (M7.4.1)** Image input — accept `.png` / `.jpg` / `.jpeg` / `.gif` / `.webp` uploads (UI mockups, whiteboard photos, design comp screenshots, sketches). **Architecture**: same two-call pattern as M7.3 OCR. Image → Claude vision `describe_image_via_claude()` → prose description → normal extract pipeline (which doesn't know or care about input modality). Trade-off vs single-call image+extract: 2x cost on image inputs (rare) but downstream stays oblivious — no per-input-type branching duplicated across five Claude call sites (extract / stream / regen / rerun / OCR). **Service** ([services/vision.py](backend/services/vision.py)): `mime_for_ext(ext)` maps file extension → Anthropic-supported media type (returns None for non-image; caller branches on that). `describe_image_via_claude(bytes, mime, *, key, model)` sends an `image` content block (base64-encoded) plus a literal "describe what you see" prompt tuned for product-requirements artifacts (covers visible elements + labels + flow + handwritten annotations + implied actors/actions). No tool use, no thinking, no user prompt suffix (M7.1) — describing is mechanical, the extraction step does the interpretation. 4K max_tokens (single-image cap). **Wiring** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): both extract routes get an image branch — when `mime_for_ext(file_ext)` returns non-None, skip `_parse_file` (would mojibake the bytes), call vision pre-pass, fill `raw_text` with the description. Records `usage_log.action="vision"` so cost surfaces alongside `extract`/`ocr`/`rerun`/`regen_*` in `/api/me/usage`. Image input REQUIRES a Claude key (no mock fallback) — fails with a 400 explaining how to add one. SUPPORTED_EXT extended to include the five image formats. **Frontend**: file input `accept` extended; visible "browse files" hint updated to mention images. No new component — image flows through the existing extraction UX (upload → loading → studio) like any text doc. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (455 modules, 149.2 KB JS — +0.05 KB, just the accept string + hint copy). **Not vision-verified** — recommend smoke (screenshot a UI mockup → drag into upload zone → confirm extraction succeeds with stories that mention the visible elements + check `/api/me/usage` shows a `vision` row alongside `extract`).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.3 (M7.3.1)** OCR fallback for scanned PDFs — fixes a real failure mode (scanned PDF upload → blank text → confusing 422). **Cause**: pypdf only extracts embedded text; image-only PDFs return whitespace + page numbers + nothing useful, then the existing M3.5 "no readable text" guard rejects with 422. **Fix** ([services/ocr.py](backend/services/ocr.py)): when pypdf yields near-empty text (`looks_like_empty(text)` — fewer than 100 alphanumeric chars; rejects whitespace + dots + page numbers without false positives), hand the raw PDF bytes to Claude as a `document` content block (base64-encoded with `media_type: application/pdf`). Claude reads PDFs natively — both embedded text and rendered page imagery — so this works for scanned, image-only, and mixed text+image documents alike. Returns plaintext via `messages.create` (no tool use, no thinking — single-turn transcribe with a simple "transcribe ALL text" prompt). The user's M7.1 prompt suffix is intentionally NOT applied to OCR — transcription is mechanical, not stylistic; custom instructions risk the model interpreting content instead of literal-transcribing. **Wiring** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): both `/api/extract` and `/api/extract/stream` get a new pre-extraction OCR-fallback block. Triggers when (file is PDF) AND (looks_like_empty) AND (effective_key set). Records a separate `UsageLog` row with `action="ocr"` so the cost surfaces in the existing `/api/me/usage` breakdown. Billed up front (before the subsequent extract call) so a failed extract doesn't grant "free OCR". Mock-mode users (no key) skip OCR — they still get the existing 422; acceptable since mock-mode + scanned PDF was always degenerate. **Trade-offs**: 8K max_tokens on the transcribe (covers ~50 dense pages — separate pagination loop deferred); two Claude calls for scanned PDFs (1 OCR + 1 extract — costs more but only fires when needed); raw_text persisted is the OCR'd text, not a hash of the original — same as text PDFs, so M5.2 click-to-source works on the OCR'd result. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (no frontend change — extraction flow handles a successful response identically whether OCR fired or not). Backend cov 54% baseline unchanged. **Not vision-verified** — recommend smoke (find a scanned PDF or print-then-scan a doc → upload → confirm extraction succeeds with reasonable structure + check `/api/me/usage` shows an `ocr` row alongside the `extract` row).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.6 (M7.6.1)** Compare two extractions — pure-UI side-by-side diff. **Backend**: zero changes — re-uses existing `GET /api/extractions/{id}` + `/versions`. The diff is fully client-side. **Diff lib** ([lib/diff.js](frontend/src/lib/diff.js)): pure functions, no React. `diffExtractions(oldRec, newRec)` returns five per-section diffs (brief / actors / stories / nfrs / gaps), each with `{added, removed, changed, unchanged}`. Generic `diffByKey()` core; per-section `keyFn`s — stories use `id` (US-NN, stable across reruns when the model preserves numbering), nfrs use `category.toLowerCase()`, gaps use a normalized `question` (whitespace-collapsed, lowercased). Unstable-key sections accept some false-positive "removed + added" pairs when the model paraphrases the key field — accepted for v1; M4.5.2 stable IDs would fix. `changedFields()` computes which top-level keys differ between two same-keyed items, so the UI can show field-level before/after instead of "this thing changed somehow". **Page** ([pages/CompareView.jsx](frontend/src/pages/CompareView.jsx)): routed at `/compare/:idA/:idB` (bookmarkable + shareable), inside the SignedIn gate. Fetches both extractions + the version chain (for "v1 → v3" labels with id-suffix fallback). Five collapsible sections, each auto-expanded when the emphasis flag is true (i.e. there are changes). Per-section count badges (`+3 -1 ~2` or `no changes`). Color-coded blocks: green for added, red for removed, amber for changed. Changed-block shows which fields differ + a `<BeforeAfter>` for each field (red strikethrough → green). Story changes filter to interesting fields (actor / want / so_that / criteria / section); pure source_quote-only changes get a tiny note instead of noisy diff blocks. **TopBar** ([components/TopBar.jsx](frontend/src/components/TopBar.jsx)): Compare link added inline to every non-current row in the existing version picker — clicking navigates to `/compare/<older>/<newer>` (sorted by version so v2 → v5 reads naturally). Picker layout reshuffled from a flat button to a row containing the switch-to button + the Compare link; quiet styling on Compare so it doesn't pull attention from the primary action. **Trade-offs taken**: one-column inline diff (vs side-by-side) — simpler, scans top-to-bottom, works on narrow viewports. No animated diff transitions — Save the design budget for M7.5 multi-doc. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (455 modules, 149.2 KB JS — +2.9 KB from M7.1, all the new page + diff lib + TopBar tweaks). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc → re-run it twice → click Compare on v1 in the version picker → confirm `/compare/<v1>/<v3>` renders with the right counts + per-story before/after).
- **2026-04-26 · M7.1 (M7.1.1; .b/.c deferred)** Custom prompt template — power users can append their own instructions to the extraction system prompt, applied to every extract / rerun / regen. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): `user_settings.prompt_suffix` nullable text column added via soft migration. 4000-char cap (mirrors comments cap — well above any real "house style" doc but below blowing up token cost). **Helper** ([services/prompts.py](backend/services/prompts.py)): tiny module with two functions — `resolve_prompt_suffix(session, user_id)` reads the saved value (tolerant of missing session / user_id / row → returns None); `join_system_prompt(base, suffix)` appends the suffix after a `# User-defined overrides` separator so the model encounters the user's overrides AFTER the defaults at reading order — important when the suffix contradicts a default rule (e.g. "use job-story format instead"). **Three Claude call sites updated**: `extract.py` (non-streaming), `services/streaming.py` (SSE), `services/regen.py` (per-section regen). All take `prompt_suffix: str | None` kwarg and pass through to `join_system_prompt`. The suffix is part of the cached system block — same user across runs hits prompt cache, different users with different suffixes don't share cache (correct). **Routes** ([main.py](backend/main.py) + [routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py)): `/api/extract` and rerun resolve the suffix in the route handler; `/api/extract/stream` resolves it in pre-flight (while the request-scoped session is still alive) and snapshots into a local before passing to the generator (which opens its own fresh session for persistence — same pattern as the M5.3 session-lifecycle fix). PUT `/api/me/settings` accepts `prompt_suffix` (empty string clears, non-empty saves; 4000-char cap enforced). **Settings UI** ([pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): new "Prompt template" section between Model and Appearance — single textarea (140px min, monospace, vertical-resize), live char count (`N / 4,000`), Save + Clear buttons, placeholder showing three concrete examples (job-story format, severity-tagging rule, actor convention). Save is disabled when nothing changed or the input is over the cap. **Trade-offs taken**: one suffix per user (vs M7.1.b multi-template) covers the 90% case — analysts have one preferred style across all extractions; multi-template is real but ships later. User-scope only (vs M7.1.c org-shared) — same reason; org-wide policy is a meaningful UX decision worth deferring. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (453 modules, 146.3 KB JS — +0.6 KB from M6.7, all the new section + form). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → Prompt template → paste "All actors must be roles, never specific people." → Save → extract a doc → confirm the output respects the constraint).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.7 (M6.7.1; .b/.c/.d deferred)** Public API tokens — long-lived bearer credentials for programmatic access (curl, Zapier, custom scripts). **Closes M6.** **Token format**: `sk_live_<base64-urlsafe(32 bytes)>` ≈ 43 chars. Prefix matches the Stripe/GitHub PAT shape so users + logs spot tokens at a glance. **Storage** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): new `ApiToken` table — `token_hash` is SHA-256(plaintext) hex, NEVER the plaintext. We don't HMAC because the input is already 256-bit random and SHA-256 of high-entropy random is not brute-forceable in any reasonable timeframe (saves us a separate secret-key dep). `prefix` + `last4` are kept clear for the `sk_live_…••••XYZK` Settings preview. `org_id` snapshots the user's active org context at create time — the token always acts in that scope, switching Clerk org later doesn't move the token (would surprise users who scripted against an org-X token). **Token service** ([services/api_tokens.py](backend/services/api_tokens.py)): `mint_token()`, `hash_token()`, `find_active_by_plaintext()`, `touch()` (best-effort `last_used_at` update — wrapped so a write failure doesn't fail the API call). **Auth integration** ([auth/deps.py](backend/auth/deps.py)): `current_user` dep extended to dispatch on the Bearer prefix — `sk_*` → token lookup → produce `CurrentUser` from the token row's `(user_id, org_id)`; anything else → existing Clerk JWT path. Same `CurrentUser` shape either way, so every downstream route (extraction, push-to-Jira, comments, share, etc.) works transparently with both credential types. Plan limits (M3.5), scope filtering (M3.3), and PostHog identification all flow through unchanged. **Routes** ([routers/api_tokens.py](backend/routers/api_tokens.py)): `GET /api/me/api-tokens` (list, includes revoked rows for audit trail), `POST /api/me/api-tokens` (mint + return plaintext exactly once), `DELETE /api/me/api-tokens/{id}` (soft-revoke — row stays as 'Revoked' so bookmarked CI configs that still send the token get a clean 401). **Settings UI**: new `ApiTokensSection` — empty state CTA → name input → submit → green "Save this token now — you won't see it again" reveal panel with the plaintext + Copy button + "I've saved it" dismiss. Create form is hidden while a freshly-minted token is on screen so the user can't accidentally create a second token before saving the first. List rows show name + `prefix••••last4` + created/last-used + Active/Revoked badge + Revoke button. Below the list: a copy-able curl snippet showing the auth shape so users see the contract without leaving Settings. New `<Key>` icon. **Schema reuse**: tokens are a separate table (different lifecycle from `IntegrationConnection` — they're our credential, not a remote system's). **Tests**: existing 26 pytest still green; the conftest's `dependency_overrides[current_user]` returns a fixed `CurrentUser`, so the new dep signature change (added `session: Session` for the token lookup path) is invisible to tests. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (451 modules, 145.7 KB JS — +1.2 KB from M6.5, all the new section + reveal panel + curl example). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → scroll to API tokens → "Create token" → name it "test" → confirm reveal panel shows plaintext → Copy → run the curl example with that token → confirm extraction returns the expected ExtractionRecord JSON).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.5 (M6.5.1; .b deferred)** Notion export — extracted stories → Notion database pages. **Auth posture**: integration token from notion.so/my-integrations, encrypted server-side. **Critical Notion permission model**: the user must explicitly share each target database with the integration via Notion's "..." menu → "Add connections" — without this the API can't see the database, no matter how broad the token. Documented in both Settings ("THEN in Notion, open each database…") and PushToNotionModal's empty state (with a link to Notion's docs). The most common "this isn't working" failure mode for Notion integrations and worth surfacing prominently. **Backend client** ([services/notion.py](backend/services/notion.py)): `NotionClient` over httpx. Two operations — `POST /v1/search` with `{filter: "database"}` (the deprecated GET /databases endpoint is gone) + `POST /v1/pages` (create). **Critical Notion API quirks handled**: 1) Databases have user-defined column schemas. The title column can be renamed (often "Story", "Item", etc., not always "Name"). We discover the title-property name from each database's schema in the search response and ship it to the frontend so the picker can submit it back unchanged on push — saves a redundant database-schema fetch on the push call. 2) Notion doesn't accept markdown — page body is a list of "block" objects (paragraph / heading_3 / bulleted_list_item / quote), each carrying a rich_text array with annotations (bold, italic). Built `_text` / `_para` / `_heading3` / `_bullet` / `_quote` helpers + `_build_blocks(story)` that renders one story as a block tree. Per-story failure isolation matches the other tracker contracts. **Schema reuse — fifth tracker, still zero new tables**. `IntegrationConnection` with `kind='notion'`, config_json `{token_encrypted, default_database_id?}`. Five trackers now confirm the row design holds for every integration we've added. **Routes**: standard CRUD + `GET /api/integrations/notion/databases` + `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/push/notion` body `{database_id, title_prop}`. **Settings**: new "Integrations · Notion" section. Test button distinguishes "401" from "200 with empty databases list" — the latter triggers a specific toast pointing at the share-with-integration step. **PushToNotionModal**: parallel modal with database picker showing `{title} (title column: {title_prop})` so the user can verify the database has the title column they expect. Empty-state has a stronger CTA than other trackers since it's the most common stuck state. **TopBar** `<PushMenu>` extended to a fifth item ("Notion" / "One page per story"). PostHog `push_to_notion_started` + `_finished {pushed, failed}`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (450 modules, 144.4 KB JS — +1.3 KB from M6.6, all the new modal + form + dropdown item). **Not Notion-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → Notion → paste integration token → save → in Notion: open a database → "..." → Add connections → pick StoryForge → back to StoryForge → Test → confirm 1+ database visible → extract a doc → Push to Notion → confirm pages appear with correct title + body blocks).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.6 (M6.6.1; .b deferred)** Slack — send unresolved gaps to a channel. **Auth posture**: Incoming Webhook URL (vs OAuth + bot token). User creates the webhook in Slack admin → channel + workspace are baked into the URL → no channel listing API call, no picker UI at push time. Right shape for "send gaps to channel" — exactly one channel per webhook. Trade-off: multi-channel = multi-webhook (M6.6.b). **Backend** ([services/slack.py](backend/services/slack.py)): `post_gaps()` builds a Slack Block Kit message — header + divider + per-gap section block (severity badge with `:red_circle:` / `:large_yellow_circle:` / `:large_blue_circle:` emoji + question + section ref + context). 50-block cap per Slack docs → we cap at 40 visible + a "+N more" footer (no extraction has produced >40 gaps in practice but the guard is cheap). Plain-text fallback for mobile notifications + screen readers. Slack's webhook contract is unusual: HTTP 200 + body literally `"ok"` on success; anything else (even 200 with `"invalid_payload"`) is failure → we check both status + body. **Schema reuse — fourth tracker, still zero new tables**. `IntegrationConnection` with `kind='slack'`, config_json `{webhook_url_encrypted, channel_label?}` (label is cosmetic — "we send to #dev-team"). **Routes** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): standard CRUD + `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/push/slack` body `{include_resolved}`. The push handler reads `gap_state` rows to compute resolved-gap indexes and filters them out (default) — opt-in `include_resolved=true` to send everything. Webhook URL prefix-validated (`https://hooks.slack.com/services/`) on save so a typo doesn't burn the first push. **Settings**: new "Integrations · Slack" section. **No Test button** (unlike Jira/Linear/GitHub) — a test post would publish a real message to the user's channel, which is the wrong UX. The first real push doubles as the test. **Push UI** ([components/PushToSlackModal.jsx](frontend/src/components/PushToSlackModal.jsx)): much simpler than the others — no picker, just a confirmation panel with channel-label preview ("Sending to #dev-team") + an "Include resolved gaps too" checkbox + Send button. Result state shows posted count. **TopBar** `<PushMenu>` extended to a fourth item ("Slack" / "Send unresolved gaps"). PostHog `push_to_slack_started` + `_finished {posted}`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (448 modules, 143.1 KB JS — +1.0 KB from M6.4, all the new modal + form + dropdown item). **Not Slack-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → paste webhook URL → save → extract a doc with gaps → Push to Slack → confirm message lands in channel with proper severity colors).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.4 (M6.4.1; .b/.c deferred)** GitHub Issues push — extracted stories → repo issues. **Auth**: Personal Access Token from github.com/settings/tokens with the `repo` scope, encrypted server-side via the same BYOK pattern. Mirrors M6.2 + M6.3's API-token posture. **Backend client** ([services/github.py](backend/services/github.py)): `GitHubClient` over httpx pointed at the v3 REST API. Two operations — `GET /user/repos?per_page=100&sort=updated` (list repos) + `POST /repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues` (create issue). **GitHub accepts markdown directly in `body`** — same as Linear, no ADF gymnastics. Clean per-status error messages — 401 (token bad), 403 (scope/permissions), 404 (repo missing or no write), 410 (issues disabled on repo), so the failure UX is debuggable. **Criteria as GitHub task list**: descriptions use `- [ ]` markdown so each acceptance criterion renders as a clickable checkbox in the issue UI — devs can tick them off as they ship. **Per-story failure isolation** matches the Jira/Linear contract; `issue_key` uses the GitHub convention `owner/repo#42` for unambiguous display in the result UI. **Schema reuse — third tracker, still zero new tables**. The M6.2 `IntegrationConnection` row composition (`scope, scope_id, kind`) handles `kind='github'`; config_json is `{api_token_encrypted, default_repo?}`. Three trackers now confirm the row design holds. **Routes** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): added `GET/PUT/DELETE /api/integrations/github/connection`, `GET /api/integrations/github/repos`, `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/push/github` body `{owner, repo}`. Same `push_extraction` rename pattern as M6.3 to disambiguate per-tracker imports. **Settings**: new "Integrations · GitHub Issues" section with single PAT input + link to github.com/settings/tokens highlighting the `repo` scope requirement. **PushToGitHubModal**: parallel component to Jira/Linear with one extra UI piece — a client-side filter input above the repo dropdown, since users with many repos benefit from typing a substring. The `<select>` uses `size={Math.min(8, ...)}` to render as a multi-line list rather than a closed dropdown, so the filter feels live. Picker value is `owner/name` (GitHub `full_name`); split on `/` before sending the push body. Deferred (M6.4.b): label picker — each label requires a per-repo list call, which would double the push round-trip count without proportional value for v1. **TopBar**: extended `<PushMenu>` to a third item ("GitHub Issues") with hint "Criteria as task list". PostHog `push_to_github_started` + `_finished {pushed, failed}`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (446 modules, 142.1 KB JS — +1.2 KB from M6.3, all the new modal + form + dropdown item). Vite size warning is now the main bundle crossing 500 KB raw — minified, gzipped 142 KB is still fine for a SaaS dashboard. **Not GitHub-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → connect with a real PAT carrying `repo` scope → Test → confirm repos load → extract a doc → Push to GitHub → confirm issue appears with task-list checkboxes for criteria).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.3 (M6.3.1)** Linear push — extracted stories → Linear issues. **Auth**: personal API key (paste from linear.app/settings/api), encrypted server-side via the existing BYOK pattern. Mirrors M6.2's API-token posture (no OAuth in v1). **Critical Linear quirk**: `Authorization` header takes the raw key, NO `Bearer ` prefix — adding it returns 401. Documented in `services/linear.py`. **Backend client** ([services/linear.py](backend/services/linear.py)): `LinearClient` over httpx pointed at the single GraphQL endpoint. Two operations — `query Teams` (list teams visible to the user) + `mutation issueCreate(input)` (create issue). **Linear accepts markdown directly in `description`** — no ADF conversion needed (unlike Jira, which forced a custom `_md_to_adf`). GraphQL errors come back with HTTP 200 + `errors[]` so we surface them explicitly. Per-story failure isolation matches Jira's `push_extraction` contract — partial success keeps the work that landed, failed rows show their error. **Schema reuse**: zero new tables. The M6.2 `IntegrationConnection` row composition (`scope, scope_id, kind`) handles `kind='linear'` for free; config_json is just `{api_key_encrypted, default_team_id?}`. Decided pattern works — when M6.4/M6.5 add GitHub + Notion, no schema churn. **Routes** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): added `GET/PUT/DELETE /api/integrations/linear/connection`, `GET /api/integrations/linear/teams`, `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/push/linear` body `{team_id}`. Same shape as Jira routes. The Jira `push_extraction` was renamed to `push_extraction_jira` on import to disambiguate from the new `push_extraction_linear`. **Settings** ([pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): new "Integrations · Linear" section parallel to Jira (`<LinearConnectionForm>`). Single API-key field — no URL or email needed (Linear key carries workspace scope). **PushToLinearModal**: parallel component to PushToJiraModal — kept separate (vs generalizing) since the picker fields differ (team_id vs project_key + issue_type) and the duplication is ~80 lines of glue, not enough to warrant a conditional abstraction. **TopBar**: replaced single "Push to Jira" button with `<PushMenu>` dropdown ("Push to…") listing Jira + Linear; same UI shape as the Export menu. Items render conditionally so a single-tracker connection still gets a clean menu. PostHog `push_to_linear_started` + `_finished {pushed, failed}`. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (444 modules, 140.9 KB JS — +1.1 KB from M6.2, all the new modal + form + dropdown). **Not Linear-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → connect with a real Linear key → Test → confirm teams load → extract a doc → Push to Linear → confirm issues appear).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.2 (M6.2.1; .b/.c/.d deferred)** Jira push — extracted user stories land as Jira issues in one click. **Auth posture**: API token (paste from id.atlassian.com), not full OAuth 3LO. Trades a polished sign-in flow for shipping today without an Atlassian developer app + Render-side OAuth config. Same encrypted-storage pattern as the Anthropic BYOK key (`services/byok.encrypt_secret`/`.decrypt_secret`). M6.2.d tracks the OAuth upgrade. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): new `IntegrationConnection` table — composite PK on (`scope`, `scope_id`, `kind`) so a user has at most one connection per integration type. v1 is `scope='user'`; org-shared (`scope='org'`) is wired into the schema for M6.2.c. `config_json` is opaque per-kind JSON; for `kind='jira'` it's `{base_url, email, api_token_encrypted, default_project_key?}`. **Backend client** ([services/jira.py](backend/services/jira.py)): `JiraClient` over httpx (no SDK — same trade-off as LSQ + Resend; simpler mocks). `list_projects()` hits `/rest/api/3/project/search?maxResults=50` (search variant returns `{values:[]}`; bare `/project` returns a list — handle both). `create_issue()` POSTs to `/rest/api/3/issue` with payload validated server-side. **Critical detail**: Jira Cloud no longer accepts plain markdown in v3 issue descriptions — only Atlassian Document Format (ADF). Built a minimal `_md_to_adf()` that handles paragraphs + bullet lists (the only shapes our story descriptions use). NOT a general-purpose MD parser; M6.2.b can swap in a proper one if formatting matters more. **Per-story failure isolation**: `push_extraction()` catches per-issue exceptions (auth, permission, custom-field validation) and records them in `failed[]` rather than aborting the batch — if 7/10 stories land cleanly and 3 hit a missing custom-field error, the user keeps the 7 + sees a per-row failure list to fix the 3. **Routes** ([routers/integrations.py](backend/routers/integrations.py)): `GET/PUT/DELETE /api/integrations/jira/connection` (token never echoed back; only `••••XYZK` preview), `GET /api/integrations/jira/projects` (live fetch — doubles as a "test connection" probe; 401 → token bad, 502 → URL/network bad), `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/push/jira` body `{project_key, issue_type}` returns `{pushed: [], failed: []}`. **Settings page** ([pages/Settings.jsx](frontend/src/pages/Settings.jsx)): new "Integrations · Jira" Section with `<JiraConnectionForm>`. Two states — connected (URL + email + ••••token preview + Test/Edit/Disconnect) and form (URL + email + token + Connect, with link to id.atlassian.com). Token never round-tripped from backend; user re-enters on Edit. **Push UI** ([components/PushToJiraModal.jsx](frontend/src/components/PushToJiraModal.jsx)): 500px modal, three states — error (no conn / token rejected / network → CTA to Settings), picker (project dropdown + issue-type select + "Push N stories" CTA), result (created issues as clickable Jira links + per-row failures with their error messages). New TopBar "Push to Jira" button (between Share + Export). PostHog `push_to_jira_started` + `_finished {pushed, failed}` for the eventual cancel/success-rate analytics. New `<Plug>` icon. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (443 modules, 139.8 KB JS — +2.3 KB from M6.1, all the modal + form + API client). **Not browser-verified or Jira-verified** — recommend smoke (Settings → connect with a real Atlassian token → Test → confirm projects load → extract a doc → Push to Jira → confirm issues appear in Jira with the right summary/description shape).
- **2026-04-26 · M6.1 (M6.1.1)** Local export menu — MD / JSON / CSV / DOCX. Studio's TopBar gains an Export dropdown replacing the single ".md" button. **MD/JSON/CSV client-side** ([lib/exports.js](frontend/src/lib/exports.js)): pure builders (no network), `downloadFile()` synthesizes an `<a download>` click in the same task as the user click so browsers don't block it as popup-during-async. JSON strips server-only fields (source_file_path, user_id, org_id) before serializing; CSV uses sectioned headers (`# Stories`, `# NFRs`, etc.) so a single file works in Excel + Sheets without a ZIP, with RFC 4180 quoting (`,`, `"`, newline → wrap-and-double). **DOCX server-side** ([services/exports.py](backend/services/exports.py)): python-docx (already installed for upload parsing) builds a structured doc — title, brief + tags, actor bullet list, per-story H2 + As-a/I-want/So-that with bold field labels + criteria bullets + italic source_quote, NFR table (`Light Grid Accent 1` style with default fallback), gap H3 + context paragraph + quote. New `GET /api/extractions/{id}/export.docx` route in [routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py) returns a `Response` with `application/vnd.openxmlformats-officedocument.wordprocessingml.document` + `Content-Disposition: attachment`. Backend chosen over a 250 KB client docx-js lib. **UI** ([TopBar.jsx](frontend/src/components/TopBar.jsx)): new `<ExportMenu>` component — Export button toggles a 180px popover with 4 menu items, each with title + hint subtitle ("Markdown / Headings + bullets" etc.). PostHog `export_clicked` event tagged with format. **Trade-offs**: NFR/gap CSV + brief CSV included (sectioned headers) so power users get everything in one file rather than a multi-file ZIP. Single button in TopBar (vs. four separate ones) keeps the action density honest. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest green; vite build clean (442 modules, 137.5 KB JS — +1.2 KB from M5.4, all the menu + builders); python-docx round-trip locally produces a 37 KB valid DOCX (ZIP magic 504b0304). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc → click Export → try each of the 4 formats → confirm files open cleanly in their respective apps).
- **2026-04-26 · M5.4 (M5.4.1 + M5.4.2)** Streaming polish. **Stop button** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js) + [App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx) + LoadingState): `extractStream` now accepts `signal` (AbortController), threaded into `apiFetch` (which already forwarded `...rest` to `fetch`, so no signature churn). App.jsx holds an `AbortController` per in-flight extraction in `useRef`; the Stop button on LoadingState calls `controller.abort()`. Abort lands in `handleExtract` as `DOMException(name='AbortError')` — distinct branch from paywall + generic error so we toast "Extraction cancelled" instead of "Failed". Backend cleanup happens automatically: when the SSE fetch disconnects, FastAPI's StreamingResponse generator unwinds, the `with anthropic.messages.stream(...)` context manager exits, and the Anthropic call drops. Tracks `extraction_failed {reason: 'aborted'}` so PostHog can show "what % of extractions did users cancel?" once enabled. **Scroll preservation** ([ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx)): when the extraction *id* changes (rerun creates a new row, or user picks a different version), the panes re-render with new content of different height — browser keeps the same `scrollTop` pixel value but it now points to unrelated content. New `useEffect` on `[extraction.id, activeTab]` scrolls the pane back to the section the user was viewing (already tracked by the existing scroll-spy). Patches + regen keep the same id, so this is a no-op for those flows (correct — they edit in place). Re-uses the existing `userClickRef` dance to suppress observer flicker during the programmatic scroll. **Vitest config fix**: M0.1.3's `e2e/` Playwright specs were getting picked up by Vitest's default discovery, breaking `npm test`. Added `exclude: ['node_modules', 'dist', 'e2e/**']` to the test config — cleanly separates the two runners. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest + 2 Playwright (locally) green; vite build clean (441 mods, 136.3 KB JS gzipped — +0.3 KB from M0 wrap, all the new abort wiring + scroll effect). **Closes M5.**

- **2026-04-26 · M0 polish (M0.1.2 + M0.1.4 partial + M0.3.3 + M0.3.4 frontend)** Closes the high-leverage M0 gaps in one bundle. **Frontend Sentry** ([lib/sentry.js](frontend/src/lib/sentry.js)): mirrors the backend pattern — silent no-op when `VITE_SENTRY_DSN` is unset; `initSentry()` called from main.jsx *before* `ReactDOM.createRoot` so import-time crashes are captured; `setSentryUser(userId, orgId)` tags events with Clerk ids (no PII — emails/names withheld), called from App.jsx via `useUser`. No `--cov-fail-under` threshold yet — would break CI on next push without giving us time to backfill tests for the streaming + regen + comments paths. Threshold can come in a follow-up once we add a few targeted unit tests. **Smoke ✓**: 26 pytest + 4 vitest, all green; vite build clean (439 modules, 135.9 KB JS gzipped — same +0.03 KB from M4.6 because Sentry's tree-shaking is aggressive when only `init` + `setUser` + `setTag` are used). **Open M0**: Playwright e2e (M0.1.3, deferred — bigger), `--cov-fail-under` threshold (M0.1.4 final), branch-protect rule (M0.2.4, repo settings only), PostHog (M0.3.5, M-sized), CONTRIBUTING + .gitignore audit + architecture diagram (M0.4.* docs polish).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.6 (M4.6.1)** Share read-only links. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): new `ExtractionShare` table — `token` (PK, opaque `secrets.token_urlsafe(16)` ≈ 22 chars), `extraction_id` FK, `created_by_user_id`, `created_at`, `expires_at` nullable (column reserved for the future "share for 7 days" flow — no UI yet), `revoked_at` nullable. Soft-revoke (not delete) so a bookmarked old URL fails closed with "revoked" rather than silently 404. **Routes** ([routers/share.py](backend/routers/share.py)): split posture in two routers. **Owner** (mounted with `_protected_deps`): `GET /api/extractions/{eid}/share` returns the active token or null; `POST` rotates (revokes existing + mints new — single-active-token model so the owner has one mental URL); `DELETE` revokes all. **Public** (mounted without auth deps): `GET /api/share/{token}` returns the same `ExtractionRecord` shape the authed routes return. 404 covers all failure modes (unknown / revoked / expired / parent deleted) — same user-facing answer so we don't leak which case it is. **Why one rotating token per extraction**: keeps the API tiny and the share UX a single button. Per-recipient labels + multi-token can come later if asked. **Frontend client** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): `getShareApi`, `createShareApi`, `revokeShareApi` (owner-side, use `apiFetch` with Clerk bearer); `fetchSharedExtraction(token)` hits raw `fetch` — deliberately bypasses `apiFetch` so we don't accidentally send a stale Clerk JWT and confuse the public route. **ShareModal** ([components/ShareModal.jsx](frontend/src/components/ShareModal.jsx)): 480px modal, scrim + Esc close. Two states: no-token shows "Create share link" CTA; with-token shows readonly URL input (auto-select on focus) + Copy button + Rotate / Revoke / Done. URL constructed client-side from `window.location.origin` — works in dev, Render preview, prod without backend host config. **ShareView** ([pages/ShareView.jsx](frontend/src/pages/ShareView.jsx)): renders the studio in read-only mode by re-using `SourcePane` + `ArtifactsPane` *without* `onUpdate`, `onPickQuote`, or comment props. The components fall back cleanly because M4.1 was designed with a read-only path from the start — that architectural decision now pays off. Minimal top bar (filename + "Shared read-only · StoryForge" + a "Sign in to StoryForge →" link). No sidebar, no rerun button, no comments. **App.jsx routing**: new `/share/:token` route placed alongside `/sign-in/*` and `/sign-up/*` (outside the `SignedIn` gate) so visitors without a Clerk account can read shared documents. **TopBar**: new `<Share>` button (between New + Export.md) wired via `onShare` callback to `setShareOpen(true)`. New `<Share2>` icon (Lucide-style 3-node silhouette) in icons.jsx. **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite green; vite build clean (131 modules, 135.9 KB JS gzipped — +2.0 KB from M4.5, all the modal + page + icon). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc → click Share → Create → copy URL → open in incognito → confirm read-only studio loads with no Clerk redirect; revoke → reload incognito → confirm 404).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.5 (M4.5.1; .2 and .3 deferred)** Comments on brief + stories. **Schema** ([db/models.py](backend/db/models.py)): new `Comment` table — `id` (`cmt_<base36-ts>_<rand6>`), `extraction_id` FK, `target_kind` ∈ {brief, story}, `target_key` (empty for brief, `US-NN` for story), `author_user_id`, `author_name` + `author_email` (denormalized at write), `body`, `org_id` (mirrors parent extraction's scope), `created_at`, `edited_at`. New table — auto-created by `create_all()`, no soft migration needed. **NFR + gap comments deferred** because their array indexes shift on M4.3 delete/reorder; need stable IDs first (M4.5.2). **Routes** ([routers/comments.py](backend/routers/comments.py)): `GET /api/extractions/{eid}/comments` returns all comments for an extraction (oldest first; frontend groups by `(target_kind, target_key)`); `POST /api/extractions/{eid}/comments` creates with body `{target_kind, target_key, body}`; `PATCH /api/comments/{cid}` and `DELETE /api/comments/{cid}` are author-only (org owners can't rewrite teammates' comments — would surprise users). 4000-char body cap. Author info from `services/email.fetch_clerk_user` at write — best-effort (Clerk failure leaves the row with empty author_name; UI falls back to `user…<id-suffix>`). Edits don't re-snap author_name (keeps "edited 2 weeks ago by old name" honest). **Frontend** ([components/Comments.jsx](frontend/src/components/Comments.jsx)): single reusable `<CommentThread>` — small button with count badge → 320px popover with thread + textarea (⌘+Enter to send). Click-outside + Esc dismiss (suppressed during in-flight network so a fast click doesn't drop a comment). Per-comment relative time (`2h ago`, `· edited`); inline Edit + Delete on own. [api.js](frontend/src/api.js): `listCommentsApi`, `createCommentApi`, `patchCommentApi`, `deleteCommentApi`. [App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx): fetches the master comments list once when an extraction opens; mutations update local state so all per-artifact popovers re-render in sync without refetching. Per-artifact filtering done in [ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx) via a `Map` indexed by `target_kind:target_key`. CommentThread mounted in the Brief `SectionHeader` action slot and inside each `StoryCard` header (next to the section ref). Threaded through `SortableStoryList` → `SortableStoryItem` → `StoryCard` so drag + comments coexist. **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite green; vite build clean (129 modules, 133.9 KB JS gzipped — +1.9 KB from M4.2, all the popover + index logic). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc, click 💬 next to a story, post a comment, refresh, verify it persists; switch users in the same org and confirm visibility).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.2 (M4.2.1)** Drag-reorder stories. Backend: zero changes — reuses M4.1's full-array PATCH. **Deps**: `@dnd-kit/core` + `/sortable` + `/utilities` (~16 KB gzipped together — acceptable for a feature this central). **Frontend** ([ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx)): split into two thin wrappers — `<SortableStoryList>` mounts `DndContext` + `SortableContext` (vertical strategy, `closestCenter` collision); `<SortableStoryItem>` calls `useSortable({id: story.id})` and forwards `listeners` to `StoryCard` as `dragHandleProps`. Wrapper-not-baked-in approach so read-only renders (legacy + future M4.6 share-link) don't pull in dnd-kit at all — keeps the read path lean. `PointerSensor` with `activationConstraint: {distance: 4}` so a click on the grip doesn't immediately start a drag (would conflict with the click-to-edit primitives nested inside the card). `arrayMove` on dragEnd → `onUpdate({stories: next})` → existing optimistic-update PATCH path. New hover-revealed grip handle on the left edge of each card (sits in the `.has-action` cluster like copy + delete); `cursor: grab` / `cursor: grabbing` for affordance. New `<GripVertical>` icon in [icons.jsx](frontend/src/components/icons.jsx) (Lucide-style 6-dot grid). - **2026-04-26 · M4.4 (M4.4.1)** "Regen stories / NFRs / gaps" buttons. Click → Claude redrafts just that section using the user's edited brief + actors + other sections as STABLE context (so M4.1 inline edits aren't blown away). **Backend** ([services/regen.py](backend/services/regen.py)): new `regen_section()` function builds a focused user message that shows non-target sections as "existing" context and the target section's current contents as "REPLACE entirely". Tool-use against per-section Pydantic wrappers (`StoriesPayload` / `NfrsPayload` / `GapsPayload` — Anthropic tool input must be an object at the root, can't take a top-level array). New `REGEN_SYSTEM` prompt is much shorter than `EXTRACTION_SYSTEM` — most of the schema instruction lives per-section in `_SECTION_META[s].instruction` so each call is focused. `max_tokens=8000` (half of full extract — single section). Mock mode returns the existing list unchanged so the UI flow is testable without an API key (intentional no-op rather than fake-shuffle to keep integration testing predictable). **Route** ([routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py)): `POST /api/extractions/{id}/regen` body `{section: "stories"|"nfrs"|"gaps"}`. Same plan gates as `/api/extract` (regen is a paid Claude call). Writes back via `setattr(row, payload.section, new_items)` then commits. Records usage with `action=f"regen_{section}"` so the existing usage breakdown table on the Account page shows regen calls separately from extract/rerun. New row is **not** created — regen is treated as a refinement of the same logical extraction, not a fork (use `/rerun` for a snapshot). **Schema** ([models.py](backend/models.py)): new `ExtractionRegenRequest` with `section: Literal["stories", "nfrs", "gaps"]`. Brief + actors aren't regenerable on purpose — small enough to inline-edit; regenerating them would lose user intent. **Frontend** ([api.js](frontend/src/api.js)): new `regenSectionApi(id, section)` returns the updated `ExtractionRecord`. [App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx): `handleRegenSection(section)` shows a `window.confirm()` first ("Replace your X with a fresh draft from Claude?"), sets `regenBusy = section`, calls the API, updates extraction state on success, refreshes the plan/usage bar, surfaces paywall errors via the existing modal. **UI** ([ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx) + [GapsRail.jsx](frontend/src/components/GapsRail.jsx)): new exported `<RegenButton>` primitive (pill, accent-toned border, `↻ Regen` label, `⟳ Regenerating…` while busy, `cursor: wait`). Mounted in the existing `SectionHeader` action slot for stories + NFRs; in GapsRail's header next to the gap counts. Disabled across all sections while any one is in flight (one Claude call at a time — keeps cost honest). **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite still green; vite build clean (124 modules, 116.3 KB JS gzipped — +0.5 KB from M4.3, all the new RegenButton + handler wiring). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (extract a doc, edit the brief, click "↻ Regen" on stories, see the call land + new stories arrive).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.3 (M4.3.1, scope expanded to add+delete)** Manual artifact creation + deletion. Buttons append a fresh empty story / NFR / gap (sequential US-NN id for stories, `{severity: 'med'}` default for gaps); per-card "×" buttons with `window.confirm()` delete. Backend: zero changes — reuses M4.1's PATCH plumbing (full-array replacement). **Frontend** ([ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx) + [GapsRail.jsx](frontend/src/components/GapsRail.jsx)): new `addStory` / `addNfr` / `addGap` / `removeStory` / `removeNfr` / `removeGap` helpers compute the new array + call the existing `onUpdate({stories|nfrs|gaps: ...})` callback. New `<AddArtifactButton>` primitive — dashed border, accent-toned, hover lifts to filled accent-soft. Delete buttons sit in the existing hover-revealed action cluster next to copy. Empty-state suppression: when editable, the "No X extracted" placeholder is hidden so the "+ Add" button isn't redundant. The new gap card auto-defaults to medium severity (most useful default — high requires confidence, low feels dismissive). Scope creep on purpose: shipping add-only without delete left the loop asymmetric (you could fill in junk but not remove it), so delete went in the same commit. **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite still green; vite build clean (124 modules, 115.8 KB JS gzipped — +0.6 KB from M4.1, all the new buttons + handlers). **Not browser-verified** — recommend smoke (click "+ Add story", fill in actor/want/so_that, refresh, verify it's persisted with sequential id).
- **2026-04-26 · M4.1 (M4.1.1)** Inline editing across the studio — every artifact field is now click-to-edit. **Backend** ([models.py](backend/models.py)): extended `ExtractionPatch` with optional `brief / actors / stories / nfrs / gaps` fields typed against the same `Brief / UserStory / NonFunctional / Gap` Pydantic types the extractor produces, so junk shapes get rejected at the route boundary instead of corrupting the JSON column. Each field is a *full replacement* (no merge) — keeps the contract trivial and the frontend always sends the intended new shape. [routers/extractions.py](backend/routers/extractions.py) `patch_extraction` applies each present field via `model_dump()` to plain dict/list for JSON-column storage. **Frontend primitives** ([components/Editable.jsx](frontend/src/components/Editable.jsx)): three small components sharing one UX contract (click → focus + select-all → Enter or blur saves → Escape discards → during-save dim). `EditableText` for short single-line fields, `EditableTextarea` for paragraphs (Cmd+Enter saves; plain Enter inserts newline), `EditableSelect` for bounded picklists like gap severity, `EditableList` for arrays of short strings (criteria, tags, actors) with per-item edit + remove + "+ Add". Read-only display gets a subtle hover-only dashed underline so editability is discoverable without screaming. [styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css): `.editable-read:hover` darkens the bg + adds an inset accent underline; `:focus-visible` outline for keyboard a11y. **Wiring** ([App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx)): new `updateExtraction(patch)` callback does optimistic local update + `patchExtractionApi` then reflects the canonical record back from the server; reverts + toasts on error. Passed as `onUpdate` to `<ArtifactsPane>` and `<GapsRail>`. [ArtifactsPane.jsx](frontend/src/components/ArtifactsPane.jsx) / [GapsRail.jsx](frontend/src/components/GapsRail.jsx) thread per-slot `onUpdate` callbacks down to each `<StoryCard>` / NFR row / `<GapCard>`, which compose `update({field: value})` from the editable primitives. Brief gains an editable summary + tag list; actors section becomes an editable list when wired (read-only when not). When `onUpdate` isn't passed (e.g. shared read-only views in a future M4.6), components fall back to the existing read-only render — same component, two modes. **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite green; vite build clean (124 modules, 115.2 KB JS gzipped + 0.4 KB sse chunk; +1.9 KB main from M5.3, all Editable primitives + wiring). **Note on testing**: backend extension tested by virtue of the existing isolation/limits suites still passing (the new fields are additive); the inline-edit UX itself isn't browser-verified — recommend manual smoke (click an actor in a story, retype, blur, see it persist on refresh) before relying in a demo.
- **2026-04-26 · M5.3 (M5.3.1 + M5.3.2 + M5.3.3, M5.3.4 deferred)** SSE streaming for the main extract flow — the studio now shows real token counts + stage progression instead of the old indeterminate "Reading…" card. **Backend** ([services/streaming.py](backend/services/streaming.py)): new sync generator `stream_extraction()` switches from `messages.parse()` (which doesn't stream) to `messages.stream()` + a tool-use definition (`emit_extraction` with `input_schema = ExtractionPayload.model_json_schema()`) so we still get validated structured output but with progress events along the way. Yields three event types: `usage` (cumulative input/output tokens, throttled — only emitted when output_tokens actually changed, so a long extraction is dozens of frames not hundreds), `complete` (full ExtractionResult + usage), `error` (single frame then stop — Anthropic auth/rate/connection errors converted, no exception propagates out). Mock mode (no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`) simulates the stream with a few `time.sleep` ticks so the frontend code path is identical mock vs live. **Route** ([main.py](backend/main.py)): `POST /api/extract/stream` keeps the same pre-flight as `/api/extract` (file size + type, project ownership, paywall via `enforce_limits`) — those still raise 4xx HTTP errors *before* the stream opens, so paywall modal logic still works unchanged. After pre-flight, returns `StreamingResponse(text/event-stream)` with `X-Accel-Buffering: no` (Render + nginx + Cloudflare honour this — frames ship as soon as we yield). Persists + records usage *inside* the generator, right before the terminal `complete` frame, so the record returned to the frontend is canonical (id + created_at) and `/api/me/plan` reflects the new usage immediately. Old `/api/extract` kept untouched — `/rerun` + future batch paths can still use it. **Frontend** ([lib/sse.js](frontend/src/lib/sse.js)): new helper `readSSE(response, onEvent)` parses the SSE wire format over `response.body.getReader()`. Why not `EventSource`? GET-only + no Authorization header support — we need both (Clerk bearer + multipart form-data). Tolerates trailing whitespace, missing `event:` line, optional space after `data:`. Doesn't parse `id:` or `retry:` (no reconnect — caller starts a new request on failure). Code-split out via `await import()` so the bundle stays lean (0.57 KB chunk loaded only when an extraction runs). [api.js](frontend/src/api.js): new `extractStream({...}, {onUsage})` wrapper. Pre-flight failures (paywall, oversize) come back as normal HTTP errors via `jsonOrThrow` — same `err.paywall` shape callers already handle. Stream-time errors arrive as SSE `error` frames and reject with the same Error contract. [App.jsx](frontend/src/App.jsx): `handleExtract` swapped to `extractStream`; new `streamUsage` state holds `{input, output, max}` updated on every `usage` event, cleared on done/error. **LoadingState rewrite**: now consumes the live `usage` and computes a stage index by comparing cumulative output_tokens against eyeballed thresholds (200 → actors, 500 → stories, 4000 → nfrs, 5500 → gaps). Stages tick from spinner → green check as the threshold is crossed. Progress bar is determinate (fill width = output/max) once the first usage event arrives; falls back to the old indeterminate slide animation for the brief "connecting to Claude…" phase. Footer line shows `in: N    out: N / max` in monospace so users see real numbers. **Why M5.3.4 deferred**: per-section progressive *render* of artifacts (StoryCards appearing as Claude writes them) needs partial-JSON parsing on the backend (probably `partial-json-parser` dep) AND a "draft mode" in `ArtifactsPane` that handles half-complete data. Heavier change, moderate added value over the current "feels alive" approach. Worth picking up later when the basics are battle-tested. **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite green; vite build clean (123 modules, 113.3 KB JS gzipped + 0.4 KB sse chunk — main bundle +1 KB from M5.2). **Note on testing**: backend unit-tested via existing isolation/limits/billing suites; the streaming generator itself isn't covered (would need mocking the Anthropic SDK's stream context manager — non-trivial). Manual smoke against a live Anthropic key recommended before relying on it in production.
- **2026-04-26 · M5.2 (M5.2.1, M5.2.2 deferred)** Click-to-source navigation. Click any source_quote on a story / NFR / gap and SourcePane smooth-scrolls to the matching passage and pulses it. **App.jsx**: new `selectedQuote` state wraps `{text, nonce}` (the nonce makes the SourcePane effect re-fire when the same quote is picked twice — useful when the user scrolls away and clicks again). `pickQuote(text)` setter passed as `onPickQuote` down to `<ArtifactsPane>`, `<GapsRail>`, and the resulting `selectedQuote` to `<SourcePane>`. **SourcePane** ([SourcePane.jsx](frontend/src/components/SourcePane.jsx)): rewritten paragraph segmenter. New `collectQuotes()` walks every story / NFR / gap and emits a flat list (with kind = story|nfr|gap for tone-coded highlights — accent / info / warn). Sorted by quote length DESC so longer quotes win when one is a substring of another. New `segmentParagraph()` finds *all* matches in a paragraph (greedy left-to-right, no overlap) — old version only found the first gap match. Each `<mark>` carries `data-quote-id` (lowercased, whitespace-collapsed, truncated to 200 chars — not cryptographic, just stable enough for `querySelector`). `useEffect(selectedQuote)` finds the first matching `[data-quote-id]`, calls `scrollIntoView({block: 'center'})`, and adds a `.quote-flash` class (force-reflow trick to re-fire the animation on repeat picks). Legacy gap.context still highlights as a fallback for pre-M5.1 stored extractions. **ArtifactsPane + GapsRail**: when `onPickQuote` is wired the `SourceQuote` chip + NFR-cell quote + gap quote render as `<button>` (focusable, keyboard-activated for free) instead of `<div>`; non-interactive fallback kept for the future where the same components might render outside the studio. **CSS** ([styles.css](frontend/src/styles.css)): `@keyframes quote-flash` — 1.1s background+ring pulse; `.quote-pick:hover` darkens the left border + ink to telegraph clickability; `:focus-visible` outline for a11y. **Why M5.2.2 deferred**: reverse direction (click a highlighted quote in source → flash the artifact card) needs stable per-artifact DOM ids and a ref into ArtifactsPane scroll. Lower value standalone; pairs naturally with M5.3 (artifacts arrive over time, so users will want to click a quote-as-it-appears and jump to its card). **Smoke ✓**: 26-test pytest suite green; vite build clean (121 modules, 112.4 KB JS gzipped — +0.7 KB from M5.1, all SourcePane logic). **Note on testing**: build passes, but no headless browser verification — eyeball check via `npm run dev` + clicking a story quote in the studio is the recommended next step before relying on this in a demo.

- **2026-04-26 · M0 (M0.1.1 + M0.2.1 + M0.2.2 + M0.3.1 + M0.3.2 + M0.3.4 backend)** Testing + CI + observability scaffolding. **Tests** ([backend/tests/](backend/tests/)): added `pytest` to requirements; new `conftest.py` pins throwaway SQLite + dummy keys *before* importing main (so `load_dotenv` can't clobber), stubs Clerk + Resend network calls in both `services.email` and `services.onboarding` (welcome_check fires on every authed touch), exposes `client` (TestClient with lifespan) + `as_user` (dependency_override on `current_user`), mints six identities (USER_A/B + USER_C/D in org-X + USER_E in org-Y + USER_A_in_org_X for self-org switch), session-scoped autouse `_ensure_schema` calls `init_db()` once so per-test cleanup fixtures (which run before any client lifespan) can DELETE from real tables.
